  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_492fdb93-170f-4289-9477-161c1ca33145'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer10954960144070401522"><b>A Maiden…</b><br/><br/>Chosen from birth to usher in a new era, Poppy’s life has never been her own. The life of the Maiden is solitary.   <span id="freeText10954960144070401522" style="display:none"><b>A Maiden…</b><br /><br />Chosen from birth to usher in a new era, Poppy’s life has never been her own. The life of the Maiden is solitary. Never to be touched. Never to be looked upon. Never to be spoken to. Never to experience pleasure. Waiting for the day of her Ascension, she would rather be with the guards, fighting back the evil that took her family, than preparing to be found worthy by the gods. But the choice has never been hers.<br /><br /><b>A Duty…</b><br /><br />The entire kingdom’s future rests on Poppy’s shoulders, something she’s not even quite sure she wants for herself. Because a Maiden has a heart. And a soul. And longing. And when Hawke, a golden-eyed guard honor bound to ensure her Ascension, enters her life, destiny and duty become tangled with desire and need. He incites her anger, makes her question everything she believes in, and tempts her with the forbidden.<br /><br /><b>A Kingdom…</b><br /><br />Forsaken by the gods and feared by mortals, a fallen kingdom is rising once more, determined to take back what they believe is theirs through violence and vengeance. And as the shadow of those cursed draws closer, the line between what is forbidden and what is right becomes blurred. Poppy is not only on the verge of losing her heart and being found unworthy by the gods, but also her life when every blood-soaked thread that holds her world together begins to unravel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10954960144070401522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3263922078" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3263922078" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3263922078?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/52941854-from-blood-and-ash">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3263922078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12411253637857305560">living in these crazy times, i was pretty certain nothing could surprise me anymore. but then JLA pulls a beyoncé and just drops this book out of nowhere, as if it were a gift delivered from the book gods themselves. <br/><br/>and this story is truly a gift that keeps on giving. there is a strong, fierce heroine and her swoon-worthy personal guard, which leads to some pretty smouldering romance. but love isnt the only emotion - this story is overflowing with bravery, suspense, loyalty, curiosity, vengeanc</span>
  <span id="freeText12411253637857305560" style="display:none">living in these crazy times, i was pretty certain nothing could surprise me anymore. but then JLA pulls a beyoncé and just drops this book out of nowhere, as if it were a gift delivered from the book gods themselves. <br /><br />and this story is truly a gift that keeps on giving. there is a strong, fierce heroine and her swoon-worthy personal guard, which leads to some pretty smouldering romance. but love isnt the only emotion - this story is overflowing with bravery, suspense, loyalty, curiosity, vengeance, and friendship. the detailed world-building presents a new, unique view of old, familiar fantasy creatures. many plot points are predictable, but not in a way that is disappointing, but rather makes the reader feel clever for catching all of the hints and signs along the way. in essence, this story has everything. <br /><br />there were some moments when i thought the ‘everything-ness’ of this story would be too much. the world-building is often given in info-dumps and i will be completely honest and say i still dont understand everything about the world, its history, and its people. but that definitely didnt stop me from loving the story or enjoying the wild ride.<br /><br />this book has truly blessed my quarantine and i hope it does the same for yours. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12411253637857305560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3263035426" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3263035426" />
    <a title="Arini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39722464-arini"><img alt="Arini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565922259p2/39722464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3263035426?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arini" href="/user/show/39722464-arini">Arini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3263035426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18048145581081862529"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586033182i/29233233._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>I hope this author never stops writing about all manner of supernatural beings bcs I’ve always had a craving for paranormal romances and she never disappoints. Even on the occasion when my rating might suggest otherwise.<br/><br/><blockquote>Coming out with a fresh from the oven NA high fantasy series, JLA surprises us with this <b>alluring</b> and <b>action packed</b> tale of fallen kingdoms on the rise, cursed bloodthirsty creatures, reluctant maidens, and steamy forbidden love affairs.</blockquote><br/><b>
  <i>Things you will love in this bo</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText18048145581081862529" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586033182i/29233233._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>3.5 Stars</b><br><br>I hope this author never stops writing about all manner of supernatural beings bcs I’ve always had a craving for paranormal romances and she never disappoints. Even on the occasion when my rating might suggest otherwise.<br><br><blockquote>Coming out with a fresh from the oven NA high fantasy series, JLA surprises us with this <b>alluring</b> and <b>action packed</b> tale of fallen kingdoms on the rise, cursed bloodthirsty creatures, reluctant maidens, and steamy forbidden love affairs.</blockquote><br><b>
  <i>Things you will love in this book:</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <u>Swoonworthy hero</u>
</b><br>Hawke is the perfect combination of <b>cocky, charming</b>, and <b>dangerous</b>. He’s <b>protective</b> of Poppy but never oversteps her boundaries. Apparently his favorite word is <i>intriguing</i>. Oh and he has dimples, which of course, Poppy loves to drool over.<br><br><b>
  <u>Kick ass heroine</u>
</b><br>Despite having lived a sheltered life, Poppy is <b>socially adept</b> and <b>skilled in combat</b>. Being a maiden means she has little to no experience in relationships. JLA made a good use of this trope by allowing her to explore and embrace her sexuality.<br><br><b>
  <u>Smoldering romance</u>
</b><br>If there is one thing you can always count on in JLA books is that the romance always <b>takes your breath away</b> and the steam has you <b>fanning yourself</b>. The chemistry is electric and the banter is top notch. I lapped it all up like a starving beast.<br><br><b>
  <u>Interesting storyline</u>
</b><br>This book has a little bit of everything—vengeance and betrayal, friendship, suspense and mystery. The climax and (non cliffhanger but surprising) ending are so adrenaline pumping and eye popping. It’s <b>the best</b> part aside from the romance obviously.<br><br><b>
  <i>Things that might hinder your enjoyment:</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <u>Slow pacing</u>
</b><br>Unfortunately, this book is very slow that I felt like I was never going to finish it. My interest kept fluctuating. There’ll be smth exciting happening once, then it’s followed by Poppy’s <b>long and self reflective inner monologue or excessive text book like infos on the world building</b>. It maintains this pattern for most of ⅔ of the book.<br><br>The last 30% of the book was truly what I lived for. It delivers <b>all the twists and turns</b> you’ve been waiting for. Sadly, it held no shocking effect for me bcs they’re fairly predictable. I think the issue with JLA books is that she drags on slow and tedious build up only to make up for it in the last ⅓ of the book.<br><br><b>
  <u>Non immersive world building</u>
</b><br>I guess what I meant to say is it needs to be just a bit more <b>convincing</b>? I have no problem with the history, lore, and beliefs system. What I think needs some touch up is the groundwork for the setting or geography of this new epic fantasy world.<br><br>I imagine creating <u>a map would be really helpful</u>. Also, instead of dumping it all out on us like the book is giving out a history lesson, I’d appreciate if the development of the world building can be more...<b>engaging</b>? So that we won’t be too overwhelmed and confused.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Fear and bravery are often one and the same. It either makes you a warrior or a coward. The only difference is the person it resides inside.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Overall, this is not at all a bad first book. I’m intrigued but still have yet to feel impressed. I do think that the author’s effort in venturing out into the high fantasy subgenre is rather successful. She managed to <b>breathe new life into old concepts</b> and make this series <b>unique</b> and <b>entirely her own</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18048145581081862529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3389504052" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3389504052" />
    <a title="She-who-must-not-be-named " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named"><img alt="She-who-must-not-be-named " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602257813p2/106473614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3389504052?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="She-who-must-not-be-named " class="user" itemprop="url" name="She-who-must-not-be-named " href="/user/show/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named">She-who-must-not-be-named </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named?shelf=all-time-favourite">all-time-favourite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3389504052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10127733264499454592"><b> Five addictive, mesmerizing, heart-rending, sexy, adrenaline-inducing stars right away! </b><br/><br/>Ever had the feeling of numbness, the feeling of having your heart break and then remade and the feeling of intensity flooding your body cells? Yeah that was me, during and after reading this book. <br/><br/>There is action and violence, passion and romance, frienship and betrayal. It is the tale about a world were anguish leaves no room for light, where the <i> Ascended </i> wield their power like a <b> poison-tipped sword </b> an</span>
  <span id="freeText10127733264499454592" style="display:none"><b> Five addictive, mesmerizing, heart-rending, sexy, adrenaline-inducing stars right away! </b><br /><br />Ever had the feeling of numbness, the feeling of having your heart break and then remade and the feeling of intensity flooding your body cells? Yeah that was me, during and after reading this book. <br /><br />There is action and violence, passion and romance, frienship and betrayal. It is the tale about a world were anguish leaves no room for light, where the <i> Ascended </i> wield their power like a <b> poison-tipped sword </b> and a kingdom that is forsaken by the gods and feared by mortals.<br /><br />Penallaphe a.k.a Poppy a.k.a <i> Princess </i> a.k.a the Maiden is never to be touched. She is forbidden to socialise, to celebrate her birthdays, go to picnics, to defend herself because she's the Maiden. She cannot live or experience anything she wants for herself without being reminded about her duty to the Gods. She doesn't have the privileges everyone around her has. But she does exactly opposite of what she's expected to do and that makes her sassier than any female protagonist I've read about. She does what she deems fit, consequences be damned. And things escalate when she meets the very attractive Royal Guard, <b>Hawke Flynn. </b> (Cheers to my 100th-something book boyfriend)<br /><br />She's strong, she's fierce, but that's not all. Poppy, despite enduring losses of people she loved dearly, walks with an air of confidence that makes you respect her amongst many other things. I loved the fact that she doesn't whine about her survivors' guilt and chooses to be better equipped and trained rather than be a liability in times of duress. Her emotional tolerance and her ability to take her shortcomings positively makes me want to hug her (I'm pretty sure I'd get stabbed even before I think about it 😂)<br /><br /><br /><b> Hawke Flynn </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Casteel Hawkethorne Da'Neer  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Of course I'm going to start with him. He is the character you will immediately love and adore. He's fast, observant, protective and if I have to steal his word<i> intriguing.</i> He is considerate and then demanding. Teasing and then cold as looming death. Violent beyond imagination but extremely tender and benign. He is the kind of boyfriend everybody hopes and deserves to have. <br /><br /> He can ignore discussions about the safety of his kingdom and other political issues just to make sure whether or not you've touched your breakfast.<br /> He will kill anyone who says something even remotely bad about you. <br />He has infinite <b> bae traits </b> and he is made up of so many layers in terms of his character complex that you'd want to unearth him and explore him deftly. <br />Oh, and did I mention he has dimples?<br /><br /><b> <u> Romance </u> </b>: <br /><br />Electric and tantalising, it is a perfect combination of sweet and steamy moments as Poppy embraces her sexuality. Hawke doesn't try to hide the fact that he's drawn to Poppy and flirts openly and they share an appealing banter. <br /><br /><br /><b>Twists: </b> <br />There are quite a few plot twists although the final twist is predictable. Trust me, it doesn't ruin the reading experience in any way. <br /><br /><b> Triggers : Mature content, violence, sex, strong language</b><br /><br /><b> <u> World building and narration </u> </b> <br /><br /><br />The initial few pages will feel slow, and the story doesn't progress much. Despite a lot of complains in this aspect, I thought it was necessary to build the world which is a bit complicated with all the new terms and to show its brutality, the gifts of the Maiden and the mystical creatures that threaten the Kingdom. <br />The narration was engrossing and portrays really well Poppy's insecurities and the feeling of being locked and suffocated for years together. <br /><br />Like I said, the story will feel dragged in the beginning but you have to trust me on this. <b> Do. Not. Let. Go. </b> Not if you want to miss out on some amazing content. A story full of court intrigue, politics, lies, infiltrations and unique creatures, <i> From Blood Amd Ash </i> is an alluring tale in all its guises and will be worth every second of your time, imploring you to to pick up the second book straight away!<br /><br />Meanwhile, *adds all of JLA's books to my tbr*</span>
  <a data-text-id="10127733264499454592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3363335164" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3363335164" />
    <a title="Mary S. R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r"><img alt="Mary S. R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597037601p2/75831724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3363335164?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary S. R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary S. R." href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r">Mary S. R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/52831247-from-blood-and-ash">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">seekers of good enemies to lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=religion">religion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=all-time-faves">all-time-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=faves">faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3363335164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5073920863503436471">(<b>4.5 ★’s</b>)<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“You’re such a bad influence,”<br/>“Only the bad can be influenced, Princess.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>That might make no sense to you but it makes perfect sense to me and to <b>Hawke who might just be my very first book crush—<i>how is that possible someone mark the date because hell has frozen over.</i></b><br/><br/>This was my very first book by JLA and I will willingly climb over your rooftop to shout at the top of my lungs and declare her an excellent writer for all and any of your neighbours to hear. Why? Because <i>From Blood and A</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5073920863503436471" style="display:none">(<b>4.5 ★’s</b>)<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“You’re such a bad influence,”<br>“Only the bad can be influenced, Princess.”</i>
</blockquote><br>That might make no sense to you but it makes perfect sense to me and to <b>Hawke who might just be my very first book crush—<i>how is that possible someone mark the date because hell has frozen over.</i></b><br><br>This was my very first book by JLA and I will willingly climb over your rooftop to shout at the top of my lungs and declare her an excellent writer for all and any of your neighbours to hear. Why? Because <i>From Blood and Ash</i> takes many of the most addictive and—<i>to use Hawke’s and my favourite word</i>—intriguing tropes and teen storytelling elements then proceeds to not only throw them all in the same pot but also add spice and her experienced touch filled with angst, working to make a memorable, mesmerising stew out of them.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Loneliness often brought with it a heavy, coarse blanket of shame, and a cloak constructed of embarrassment.</i>
</blockquote><br>I believe what made this book a favourite and an obsession for me is the clever fact that the pieces gathered from all over the YA and NA genre are not simply inserted next to one another, but spun around to tread a fresh path and well-developed to stand out of the thin, flat pages boldly. <b>From a sheltered, caged Maiden that is in truth a secretly rebellious skilled warrior, to a charming, shameless, cunning vicious guard love interest who cheers for her as she fights and stands next to her rather than in front of her, to the potent and intoxicating feeling of raging anguish thoroughly lacing the tale, JLA has created an iconic, unbelievably hot, and forbidden enemies to lovers dynamic in a nearly flawless paranormal romance that I gleefully let drown me.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“The truth is not designed to ease fears,” Vikter responded.<br>“Is that why we tell lies, then?”</i>
</blockquote><br>But the author’s best decision, in my eyes, was writing FBaA as a new adult book. No, not because of all the steamy tension (<i>though there’s also that</i>), but because <b>this genre let Poppy’s struggles with her gilded cage, lacking freedom, stolen choice, and the inherent yet quiet theme of religion in <i>From Blood and Ash</i> to be opened without being glossed over and left unexplored.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>From Blood and Ash<br>We Shall Rise.</i>
</blockquote><br>Evidently and unfortunately, I’m rather efficient at predicting things (<i>if I say so myegoisticself, and I do</i>) and it did not help that the reveals <i>were</i> predictable; in fact, if you draw a Venn diagram of every single twist in FBaA, big and small, and every single prediction of mine, big and small, the circles wouldn’t just overlap—they’d be virtually the same. The phenomenon here though is how me seeing it all coming did not take away even 0.00000001% of my enjoyment. <b>What it truly felt like was rereading a favourite book.</b><br><br>It makes sense: the plot starts ingenuously and remains exciting in its small bumps instead of grand turns, the UST-filled dynamic is perpetually perfect and deliciously inebriating, the characters are all precisely my type in their insanity (<i>even side characters like Tawny who you’ll find saying things like, “My hormones are always clouding my rational thought, thank you very much.”</i>), the action scenes are well written and not impossible, and the book does indeed enjoy being deadly and killing its characters in the most emotional way possible (<i>I cried so many times I swear—though my <a href="https://open.spotify.com/playlist/4dKbR1VVszCiLd4yofO3QJ" rel="nofollow noopener">book playlist</a> might also be to blame</i>).<br><br>Death with dignity, dignity in death; <i>From Blood and Ash</i> certainly killed me without giving me the courtesy. Damn all cliffhangers to hell.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Death is like an old friend who pays a visit, sometimes when it’s least expected and other times when you’re waiting for her. It’s neither the first nor the last time she’ll pay a visit, but that doesn’t make any death less harsh or unforgiving.”<br>Death always found a way in.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>CW</u>
</b> ➾ graphic mature content, explicit language, sexual assault, abuse, caning, sexism, loss of loved ones, blood and violence<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600276971i/30115246._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Obsessed Thumbs Up: <i>Romance</i></u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I hate you.”<br>“No, you don’t.”<br>“And I’m about to stab you,” I warned. “In a very violent manner.”<br>Concern flickered across his face as he lowered the book. “Now that, I believe.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Read the above quote and tell me that’s not one of <i>the</i> most romantic things you have ever read. No, <i>tell me</i>.<br><br>Thinking on it though, maybe no one should evaluate the romantic-ness of anything based on the opinion of a deeply sick and sociopathic aromantic whose fave dynamics are similar to <b>a savage, furious sparring match where the partners are striving to draw first blood and the chemistry is all about the quandary of wanting and abstaining, and is probably not the paragon of a healthy relationship.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1604124510i/30312566._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Credit: <a href="https://instagram.com/theclever.crow" rel="nofollow noopener">Catherine Crowley</a>
</blockquote>
</blockquote><br>Why do I love them? I love how he’s a lethal killer and she’s (<i>disturbingly enough</i>) drawn to it. I love how <i>she</i>, too, is a skilled fighter and pushes herself to work harder and not be bested by him. And oh I love how he <i>sees</i> her and <i>challenges</i> her and never underestimates her. I love how <i>insane</i> they both are. Happy now?<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“When you listen to me, I think the stars will fall.”</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600276971i/30115246._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Swooning Thumbs Up: <i>Hawke Flynn</i></u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“You’re ridiculous,” I sputtered.<br>“What I am is intrigued.”</i>
</blockquote><br>How can you love someone so much and yet want to kill them so badly? I don’t know but I think Poppy does, because I believe we share that urge to constantly stab Hawke Flynn with a sharp dagger. Honestly? Hawke’s cunning charming audacious insufferable arrogant vengeful killer swaggering put me in mind of Rhysand from <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2607459551" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Mist and Fury</a>
</i> except I love Rhys more as one would an adorable misunderstood puppy while Hawke might just have claimed the place of my first (<i>or second?)</i> book crush. To put it simply, <b>Hawke is a less mushy more cutting-blade version of Rhys, which is just my gig—the less mush the better.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600276971i/30115246._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Relieved Thumbs Up: <i>Penellaphe Balfour</i></u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Wasn’t that what living meant? Taking more than a sip here and small bite there. It was all about gulping and swallowing as much as you could.</i>
</blockquote><br>First, I would like to thank the gods of publishing industry as we seem to be getting blessed with so many unique, captivating badass female leads (<i>or maybe it’s just me and I’m gravitating towards a certain type of book</i>). Secondly, I would like to thank JLA for blessing me with <b>Poppy who is not just “another strong female MC” and actually <i>deserves</i> the title.</b><br><br><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1604920256i/30354418._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Credit: <a href="https://instagram.com/jemlin_c" rel="nofollow noopener">Jemlin</a>
</blockquote><br>Yes, she might be the opposite of all the traits her namesake represents (<i>Penellaphe, the Goddess of Wisdom, Loyalty, and Duty—bearing another type of rare strength</i>) she is strong and courageous all the same. This girl, who has endured abuse and pain and chains most of her life, kept quiet and steady, swallowing her pain and keeping her chin up, is the epitome of strength; later falling over the edge and into the unstoppable well of rage does not change that. Becoming an extreme, violent, wild, vengeful, deadly, occasionally irrational tornado does not change that, because it is her <i>right</i>. To protest and refuse being a helpless pawn is her <i>right</i>. <b>I cheered as she exploded, fell in love with her only when she snapped. And her every action and thought and aspect of story supported and <i>showed</i> this vicious strength and I appreciate how JLA’s words were not empty.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“And your scars? They are a testament to your fortitude. They are proof of what you survived. They are evidence of why you are here when so many twice your age wouldn’t be. They’re not ugly. Far from it. They’re beautiful, Poppy.”</i>
</blockquote><br>With Poppy whose choice, whose future was long ago taken away, FBaA delves into the traditional expectations society has of women such as the “innocence” and value of virginity over every other part of person’s character, and digs deep, not being satisfied with brushing the surface. With Poppy who was not allowed to <i>want</i> or <i>need</i> and was thrown in a cage of vipers, never safe and never free, JLA takes note of all that people have and take for granted, <b>peppering this book of romance with reality.</b><br><br>With Poppy, JLA shows gradual change and cutting of chains through determination and dreams and NOT because of falling in love with a guy.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>A Maiden doesn’t question the gods’ plans. She has faith in them without knowledge of them.<br>Maybe I truly wasn’t worthy of being a Maiden, because I found it hard to have faith in anything without knowledge of it.</i>
</blockquote><br>To be honest, I was hesitant about reading the tale of “a sheltered, clueless girl” falling in love with her “protector” but man am I relieved that Poppy was not that; she resisted being “sheltered and clueless” at every turn and awed me with her fierceness, clear intelligence (<i>which was no less marred by her sometimes idiotic decisions rooted in emotions or lack of cunning</i>), and relentless curiousity (<i>that was never stopped by fear</i>). <b>It’s brave and compassionate Poppy’s of the world who make me remember why I loved Gryffindors.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Fear and bravery are often one and the same. It either makes you a warrior or a coward. The only difference is the person it resides inside.”</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600276971i/30115246._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Sad Semi Thumbs Down: <i>World Building</i></u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“May Rhain escort you to paradise,” I whispered, wiping the blood from my dagger on a small towel that had been draped over the end table. “And may you find eternal peace with those who have passed before you.”</i>
</blockquote><br>No, the downfall of <i>From Blood and Ash</i> was not being predictable because really who cares life is predictable, it was its world building—no, not its <i>world</i> but the <i>building</i> of its world.<br><br><b>At first glance, you would find the book confusing and think it’s complicated, but that’s not the case; at least, it <i>could</i> have been the case because the world JLA has created is, in essence, complicated, but not on the page. Instead, it’s akin to being given 10 pieces of a 100 piece puzzle you don’t know the eventual picture of to put them in their right places, frame it, and gladly hang it on your wall and go about your day.</b> I mean, <i>who the fuck does that?</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Some truths do nothing but destroy and decay what they do not obliterate. Truths do not always set one free. Only a fool who has spent their entire life being fed lies believes that.”</i>
</blockquote><br>FBaA attempts to walk the <i>there are two sides to every story</i> path and grossly fails, neglecting one side of the story so thoroughly that you have no choice but to accept the other side and can’t understand what the characters are even conflicted about as, in all honesty, one side makes absolutely zero sense. This is a very lacking approach and takes away tremendously from the book’s potential. I know, you’re going to say “but you didn’t criticise the world in, say, <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2968223053" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadows Between Us</a>,</i> a fantasy romance with barely any world building,” and that’s because Tricia Levenseller decided what she wanted to write and didn’t make any claims to other aspects, while JLA chose to go there but, sadly, tripped.<br><br>What this lead to was a world with a jumble of fantastic ideas and spins on paranormal creatures and no glue to hold them together whatsoever. Only at the very end of the book does the glue of sense grace us with its presence and even then explanations and rules are vague, making the world disjointed and odd but not in the good odd way I cherish.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600276971i/30115246._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My issue with JLA’s world building nearly stopped me from shelving <i>From Blood and Ash</i> as not just a fave but an all-time fave. Fortunately, Hawke and Poppy and their romantic bloodsport so helplessly possessed my heart that I was all but an adoring acolyte.<br><br><br><b>
  <u>Companions</u>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>Book series playlist:</i>
</b> <a href="https://open.spotify.com/playlist/4dKbR1VVszCiLd4yofO3QJ?si=13bpf0QYSdeQGKn0k729GA" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify URL<br><br><blockquote><blockquote><blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600247212i/30113020._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></blockquote></blockquote></blockquote></a><br><b>
  <i>Books in series:</i>
</b><br>➴ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3639424420" rel="nofollow noopener">The Red Pearl Bonus Scene</a> (Blood and Ash, #0.5) ★★★✯☆<br>➴ From Blood and Ash (Blood and Ash, #1) ★★★★✯<br>➴ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3547670484" rel="nofollow noopener">A Kingdom of Flesh and Fire</a> (Blood and Ash, #2) ★★★★✯<br>➴ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3551376222" rel="nofollow noopener">The ​Crown of Gilded Bones</a> (Blood and Ash, #3) ☆☆☆☆☆</span>
  <a data-text-id="5073920863503436471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3277840404" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3277840404" />
    <a title="• Lindsey Dahling •" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26262267-lindsey-dahling"><img alt="• Lindsey Dahling •" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578858809p2/26262267.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3277840404?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="• Lindsey Dahling •" class="user" itemprop="url" name="• Lindsey Dahling •" href="/user/show/26262267-lindsey-dahling">• Lindsey Dahling •</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26262267-lindsey-dahling?shelf=bitchin">bitchin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26262267-lindsey-dahling?shelf=lindsey-marti-book-club">lindsey-marti-book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3277840404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13153936721611441118"><i>Holy shit. </i>I almost DNF this at 16%. I was bored. There were info dumps everywhere. The narrator was blah. The plot wasn’t moving. Goodness, even the TIME IN THE BOOK wasn’t moving. Pretty sure at 16% not even 24 hours had passed in this book world. I told myself I would jump ship if this did not improve by the 20% mark.<br/><br/>Damn did it improve. I’ve never been so glad I didn’t jump ship. (Okay, that’s a lie. I was also really glad I didn’t jump ship during season 5 of The Vampire Diaries.)<br/><br/>Suddenly..</span>
  <span id="freeText13153936721611441118" style="display:none"><i>Holy shit. </i>I almost DNF this at 16%. I was bored. There were info dumps everywhere. The narrator was blah. The plot wasn’t moving. Goodness, even the TIME IN THE BOOK wasn’t moving. Pretty sure at 16% not even 24 hours had passed in this book world. I told myself I would jump ship if this did not improve by the 20% mark.<br><br>Damn did it improve. I’ve never been so glad I didn’t jump ship. (Okay, that’s a lie. I was also really glad I didn’t jump ship during season 5 of The Vampire Diaries.)<br><br>Suddenly...<br>—there was dialogue. And not just dialogue—witty banter.<br>—the narrator SHOWED she was a badass.<br>—there was a male lead who did something other than be gorgeous.<br>—the villains started to make their presence known in despicable ways that made my blood boil 😡💯👏🏻.<br>—we had side characters who were super likable.<br>—we had a slow burn romance that didn’t feel forced.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1563071529ra/27824069.gif" width="429" height="208" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’ll be honest—witty banter alone will keep me reading. But then LITERALLY ALL OF THE OTHER TROPES I ADORE showed up and I was just 😏😏😏😏😏😏😏😏😏😏 for the rest of the book.<br><br>I finished about 5 minutes ago, so I’m not even sure I’m typing coherent sentences right now. The book is THAT good. <br><br>Just push through the boring beginning. You can do it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1564588696ra/27918712.gif" width="480" height="267" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13153936721611441118" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3255401036" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3255401036" />
    <a title="TheBibliotheque ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36566317-thebibliotheque"><img alt="TheBibliotheque ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518728337p2/36566317.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3255401036?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheBibliotheque ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheBibliotheque ♡" href="/user/show/36566317-thebibliotheque">TheBibliotheque ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36566317-thebibliotheque?shelf=2020-faves">2020-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36566317-thebibliotheque?shelf=faves-fantasy">faves-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3255401036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16300112210322525358"><i>"You're an absolutely stunning, murderous, little creature."</i><br/><br/>YO. YOOOO. I have been keeping quiet about this book FOR A MONTH and all this contained fangirling energy almost makes me implode.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468353604ra/19696061.gif' width='395' height='219' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I know you know me and my neverending and neverdying love for Jen's books. So imagine the array of emotions that passed through my body when I was given the chance to read her upcoming novel early (elation, HAPPINESS, joy) but I was asked not to speak a word of it (contained fangirling, frustration, yearning)</span>
  <span id="freeText16300112210322525358" style="display:none"><i>"You're an absolutely stunning, murderous, little creature."</i><br><br>YO. YOOOO. I have been keeping quiet about this book FOR A MONTH and all this contained fangirling energy almost makes me implode.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468353604ra/19696061.gif" width="395" height="219" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I know you know me and my neverending and neverdying love for Jen's books. So imagine the array of emotions that passed through my body when I was given the chance to read her upcoming novel early (elation, HAPPINESS, joy) but I was asked not to speak a word of it (contained fangirling, frustration, yearning).<br><br>Well, NOW this book I have been dying to yell and scream about is finally OUT! Yes, Jen really did sneak that one out on you. But now, I repeat-NOW, it is out in the world and we can finally talk about it. I can yell about it. Fangirl. Swoon. Fight you over Hawke (which - mark my words - I will).<br><br>From Blood &amp; Ash is Armentrout’s take on high fantasy. It’s current, it’s filled with banter and fun and it integrates elements that we are all familiar with, giving them that JLA spin. Creatures, forgotten civilisations, enchanted forests, gods, royalty, all if it! But I’ll be 100% honest, at first it did feel like a little bit too much, perhaps the unfamiliarity of the world, or perhaps the building didn’t reach my expectations. And this may happen to you too, so my advice is HOLD ON TO IT.<br><br>Because THE ROMANCE. THE LOVE INTEREST. It was EVERYTHING<br>Above the fact that this is a new fantasy series, if there was something - one thing - that shocked me about FB&amp;A that was its love interest. Hawke. I know, you're probably thinking that I do love and adore all heroes created by that beautiful mastermind that is Armentrout, and you are right. But listen up. Hawke will catch you completely off guard. He was a love interest like no other love interest. Cheeky, protective, infuriately sexy and a puzzle you'll want to piece together. Just trust me on that.<br><br>And the steam? Yeah, you'll want to trust me on that too.<br><br>SO. If you think you are ready for From Blood and Ash, think again. Jennifer has woven a new fantasy universe that will leave you reeling. Filled with action, heart wrenching twists and the most delicious romance, this unputdownable novel comes with a warning: keep a fan close by, because the temperatures are about to rise.<br><br>Rating: 4.5/5<br><br>*I received an ARC from the author in exchange for an honest review.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3257777112" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3257777112" />
    <a title="Sapir Englard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5822606-sapir-englard"><img alt="Sapir Englard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596445110p2/5822606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3257777112?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sapir Englard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sapir Englard" href="/user/show/5822606-sapir-englard">Sapir Englard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3257777112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4975465723917436126">This review contains spoilers. Just saying.<br/><br/>Rating: 1.5 stars.<br/><br/>There should be a new adult fantasy genre called Maas Fantasy, after Sarah J Maas. That genre would be full of pretty people, non original world building, out-of-genre writing that can be either really bad or even worse, love interests that all they do is be horny assholes yet get a sway with because they’re hOT, and the use of the terms MALES and FEMALES.<br/><br/><br/>I’ve read a lot of books by Jennifer L. Armentrout. I don’t think she’s a bad aut</span>
  <span id="freeText4975465723917436126" style="display:none">This review contains spoilers. Just saying.<br /><br />Rating: 1.5 stars.<br /><br />There should be a new adult fantasy genre called Maas Fantasy, after Sarah J Maas. That genre would be full of pretty people, non original world building, out-of-genre writing that can be either really bad or even worse, love interests that all they do is be horny assholes yet get a sway with because they’re hOT, and the use of the terms MALES and FEMALES.<br /><br /><br />I’ve read a lot of books by Jennifer L. Armentrout. I don’t think she’s a bad author - but her writing style and concepts belong more to the contemporary romance area. She writes good sex scenes, builds up just the right amount of sexual tension between the two main characters, and this is why I think her Wait For You series is the best, since it represents these elements down to the T.<br /><br />However, I read fantasy and paranormal series from Armentrout, and even though I’m disappointed every time anew, I keep falling for it. I actually thought this book would be different from her Covenant and White Hot Kiss series. Especially since I had faith she learned from her SUPER OBVIOUS PLAGIARISM in Half-Blood, a matter that still makes me mad to this day, but I was willing to move past that. I completely was.<br /><br />Then comes this book.<br /><br />This book starts with an info-dump, a writing device that becomes worryingly more and more common nowadays within the fantasy writers. I have to admit, I skipped them all, because YAWN - I don’t want to read about your marvelous world on the first chapter without any suspense as to what’s going on. It’s so Urban Fantasy, and I’m OVER IT.<br /><br />Next, after everything is shoved down my throat (although, as admitted above, I skipped it all, returning whenever there was quotation marks that indicated something happening) we have a disturbing scene in which we are supposed to believe that what’s-her-face is that sheltered Maiden written about in the book summary as she encounters the love interest, Hawke, whose behavior was COMPLETELY CREEPY AND DISTURBING. The banter was weak, POP-Tart was acting like an idiot, and it all read like a scene straight out from an urban fantasy book, only instead of a club we have some weird version of a love motel.<br /><br />Moving on, I skipped a lot of the beginning. It was dull, the murder-mystery thing it had going on was boring, and I was not at all enthralled with either Pop-tart or her honey bunny in the making. I also hated that Tawny fell into the Mandatory POC trope since she had absolutely zero influence on the plot, and was there to fluff the feather of the BEAUTIFUL WHITE CHARACTER. I mean, COME THE FUCK ON. Can we NOT?<br /><br />Also, there’s a recurring theme in Armentrout’s books: the villains are very BAD, and the good people are very GOOD. There’s no in between. No morally gray characters. No depths to her villains. Absolutely nothing. And it pisses me off, especially since the audience she aims for is no longer an idiot.<br /><br />Now let’s talk about Pop-tart and Hawke, since they were supposedly the least shallow of the rest. Pop-tart was annoying, stupid, “sassy”, “mouthy”, ethereally beautiful with sCArS, and if that sounds familiar, it could be because: 1) It’s every main character in Armentrout’s books, and 2) It’s the YA/NA Quirky Protagonist Syndrome (QPS?) that can be seen in many book of this genre. The “mystery” of this book was so dumb, so predictable, every plot twist got a complete YAWN from me, and yet Pop-tart was such an imbecile, not getting any of it until she was told it all. And Hawke called her “smart”. Cue my facial question mark.<br /><br />Which is, by the way, ANOTHER recurring theme in Armentrout’s book: STUPID HEROINES &amp; PREDICTABLE PLOT POINTS. Her mysteries are always pushed into your face from page 1, and it’s all because of her overly-thick foreshadowing that people can tell them from miles away. The whole point of foreshadowing is to be SUBTLE, but I guess the readers are too stupid, right, Armentrout? Also, the fact the basic bitch heroines don’t get it is a cause for an endless migraine.<br /><br />Next, Hawke. From a writer’s POV, I understand what Armentrout was going for when writing him; the sexy, hot, mysterious guy who then, supposedly, becomes morally gray, and wicked, and hot, and super good in bed, and, of course, immortal, and fights for the TRUE GOOD SIDE and so forth. What she ended up with was a horny asshole, and I’m talking about the last part of the book, after all, or most, at least, has been revealed to the dumb-fucker who is Pop-tart. After being betrayed, you would expect Pop-tart to be rational, but no, he’s HOT, and she’s IN LOVE with him, so LET’S SEX IT UP, BABY!<br /><br />Ew. Ew. Ew. I found everything that happened in the last few chapters revolting, and not in the cute, sexy way Armentrout was aiming for, but in the call-the-police way.<br /><br />Let’s go back to Pop-tart for a moment. For someone who’s supposedly been sheltered her ENTIRE LIFE, she surely doesn’t act like that. She’s supposed to, but she doesn’t, and that’s just lazy writing right there, but again, I really shouldn’t have expected anything from this book in the first place. Still, the sex scenes, while hot - because Armentrout is great at writing those - and the sex-times before that, Pop-tart acted as if she knew more than she should, which leads me to the point of that erotic novel she was reading - like, she’s sheltered and a virgin. WHY WOULD THERE BE A BOOK LIKE THIS WITHIN HER GRASP IN THE FIRST PLACE?! But again, high fantasy is not what it used to be, and consistency and good worldbuilding is a complete nonsense, am I right?<br /><br />Anyway, Pop-tart and Hawke were completely annoying, and I don’t like them at all. I especially don’t like the ending, about Pop-tart being a hybrid because that’s just Armentrout ripping off her own work - Wicked ending, much? - and basically giving in to the whole Special Snowflake trope. Also, Hawke whisking her away to MARRY when she’s EIGHTEEN is fucking revolting.<br /><br />Now let’s talk writing. This was not a high fantasy writing. While I don’t need a Game of Thrones type of writing, because that’s too heavy even for me, there’s something about setting the tone and air of the book, and when you write, “I totally got that” it reads as a millennial, not an eighteen-year-old sheltered girl in a fantasy land. <br /><br />The usage of our-world words pissed me off. You can’t drink Champagne in your fantasy world - because Champagne is a place in France, and if your world has no France, then there will be no Champagne! Call it wine or something, but at least be accurate! It’s like using a Dijon mustard or eating burgers!<br /><br />The terms Males and Females reared their fugly head in this book, too, which is a wink to SJM that I really didn’t appreciate, and also let me in to the fact Armentrout was probably reading SJM books, which is disturbing, and will probably try to rip off one of them because I still can’t forgive the Half-Blood plagiarism issue.<br /><br />Other terms that struck me out as too modern: Earth, sweater, and many, many more.<br /><br />Now let’s talk about the names. Masadonia? Atlantia? Can’t you be at least original and not rip off places of our REAL WORLD unless there’s a GOOD REASON for you to do that? Like, come the fuck on. Also Changing words in people’s names with E doesn’t make them fantasy: Vikter instead of Viktor, Malessa - Malissa, Teerman - Tearman. So just stop. Also, Penellaphe Balfour? Really? REALLY? In addition, there’s King Malec and Prince Malik, both of which translates directly into “King” which is stupid, and vamprys, which is a fancy way to write vampires, and Casteel, which is a type of Beer so I won’t even start.<br /><br />Other rip-offs: Pop-tart’s magical ability is not original at all. It’s like Sascha Duncan from Psy/Changeling and the Dementors from HP made a baby, and tada! A NEW POWER WAS BORN! Not. Which leads me to the point of the vampire-ish creatures of this so-called world. I mean, COME THE FUCK ON. You have the option to create new races and you go with VAMPIRES? AGAIN? COME. ON.<br /><br />One last thing: a nugget that made me giggle. Pop-tart said, “How had I not seen him for what he was? Could I be that foolish? Or was he simply that clever? Probably both.” Brah, you were stupid. That’s all there is to it.<br /><br />I can go on forever, but this review is long enough. Anyway, if you enjoyed this book, and this type of nonsensical writing and worldbuilding and plot is your thing, good for you. For me, it’s just pissing on everything the high fantasy genre stands for, much like SJM in that way.<br /><br />That’s my take on it. Hopefully, I won’t forget the content of this book by the time the next one comes, which will lead me to not read it, but I’m doubtful. Oh, well.<br /><br />(P.S The half star is for the sex scenes because when something IS good, it deserves the credit).<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4975465723917436126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3526794695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3526794695" />
    <a title="Sofia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/114413220-sofia"><img alt="Sofia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606141536p2/114413220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3526794695?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofia" href="/user/show/114413220-sofia">Sofia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=a-man-saves-the-day">a-man-saves-the-day</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=how-was-this-published">how-was-this-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=your-typical-ya-fantasy">your-typical-ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=i-am-disgusted">i-am-disgusted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=failed-romance">failed-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=mary-sue">mary-sue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=misplaced-hype">misplaced-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=new-level-of-trash">new-level-of-trash</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=idek-anymore-guys">idek-anymore-guys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3526794695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10941263401578012023">Hello hello. Welcome to another episode of Sofia Hates Everything. Today's guest is From Blood and Ash, or as I like to call it, From Mud and Trash. The hype deceived me once again. <br/><br/><br/>This book follows Poppy, the Maiden, chosen one of the gods, whose Ascension day is coming soon. First of all, what is the Ascension? I have no idea. Why does Poppy exist? Where do the Ascended go? Why are they chosen? How are they chosen? What is their point? Why is there a Maiden? I can answer none of these questio</span>
  <span id="freeText10941263401578012023" style="display:none">Hello hello. Welcome to another episode of Sofia Hates Everything. Today's guest is From Blood and Ash, or as I like to call it, From Mud and Trash. The hype deceived me once again. <br /><br /><br />This book follows Poppy, the Maiden, chosen one of the gods, whose Ascension day is coming soon. First of all, what is the Ascension? I have no idea. Why does Poppy exist? Where do the Ascended go? Why are they chosen? How are they chosen? What is their point? Why is there a Maiden? I can answer none of these questions, and that's a problem. <br /><br /><br />Poppy's real name is... drum roll please... Penellaphe Balfour. *chokes* Apologies to all of you named Penellaphe, but that is some serious tongue-twister. And there are also characters named Malessa, Vikter, Hawke... basically, just add an "e" whenever there should be another vowel. Or add an "e" because why not. Wait, I found an answer to those previous questions. Poppy's the Maiden BECAUSE WHY NOT, why do we even need a reason? I'm just going to accept this and move on. <br /><br /><br />Speaking of horrendous names, the world of this book is called Masadonia. Which is literally Macedonia, only speshul. And the bad guys are called Atlantians, because they're from Atlantia, which is totally not something I've heard before. The baddest baddie's name is The Dark One, because, again, WHY NOT. Why shouldn't an author put some effort into their fantasy world? Why shouldn't they at least try to incorporate some atmosphere? I ask for too much. <br /><br /><br />Because Poppy's the Maiden, she lives a very sheltered life. She's not allowed to talk to anyone, even her ladies in wait. She lives behind a veil until her Ascension day. There is no problem with this. The problem I have is with how it is done. She's supposed to be very sheltered and naive, but she's not. She knows everything about everything, talks in slang, is perfectly sociable. This makes no sense. Take <i>Cress</i> by Marissa Meyer, for example. Cress has lived in a satellite her whole life, and has never interacted with another person. And she ACTS like it. She ACTS like she's lived a sheltered life. Poppy doesn't. <br /><br />Poppy is supposed to be the sassy, special heroine with ✨scars✨ and a ✨dagger✨ but she's just so cringy. Her "banter" is disgustingly predictable and typical, it's not even funny. Hawke called her "smart," which confuses me. She is unable to see what is right in front of her. She is not like other girls because she has fewer brain cells. <br /><br /><br />I'm not even going to address the biggest issue with this book until the end, or else I will quite literally explode. And I don't want to make a mess. <br /><br /><br />So I'll move on to THE WRITING. I haven't read anything THIS BAD in a very long time. And that's saying something. I think I'm allergic to ellipses, because I have a headache after they were used MULTIPLE TIMES, EVERY PAGE, WHERE THEY AREN'T EVEN NEEDED. Behold. (The page numbers are for the ebook, large font.) <br /><br /><i>"I... I would face the Duke's displeasure."</i> pg. 46<br /><i>"I felt like... like I was being watched."</i> pg. 58<br /><br />Wait, this is my favorite one: <br /><i>"Tonight was about living, about...not being up all night, unable to sleep, alone and feeling like...like I had no control, no...no idea of who I was other than what I was."</i> pg. 40<br /><br />THREE TIMES. IN A SINGLE SENTENCE. AND THAT'S ON TOP OF UNNEEDED REPETITION THAT MAKES POPPY SOUND LIKE SHE HAS A SERIOUS STUTTER <i>IN HER THOUGHTS.</i> Sure, talk that way, but don't THINK that way. <br /><br /><br /><i>"The music was...it was like nothing I'd heard before."</i> pg. 59<br /><i>"I... I hadn't heard that."</i> pg. 61<br /><br />I skipped many pages in between the last one and this next one, because a) I skimmed that part, and b) I don't want to type them all, for the sake of my fingers. <br /><br /><i>"Did you... did you recognize her?"</i> pg. 255<br /><i>"Did you... did you see her?"</i> pg. 256 (literally the next page) <br /><i>"When will... when will Rylan be put to rest?"</i> pg. 322<br /><i>"I... I couldn't sleep."</i> pg. 335<br /><i>"The contrast of the fan and gown was... atrocious and also interesting."</i> pg. 452<br /><i>"What... what if he was actually here?"</i> pg. 463<br /><br /><br />I just picked the most horrendous ones. There are plenty more, I promise you. I think you get the idea.<br /><br /><br />And then there are these moments that just made me cringe: <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Air whooshed from my lungs, and the entire Hall seemed to fade away, going silent as we stared at one another.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Girl, it was not that dramatic, and you know it. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Rylan had died because of me.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Stop taking responsibility for everything. The world does not revolve around you, honey. People die, because that's what people do. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>His stare was piercing as if he could see not only through me, but into me... It had to be his eyes and their color. Such a strange, stunning golden hue.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Is he even a YA love interest if he doesn't have speshul eyes that stare into your soul? *bangs head on table* I am done. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>A well of pain hidden behind a teasing and charming personality.</i>
</blockquote> <br /><br />We get it, he's angsty. Maybe he didn't drink his coffee this morning. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Poppy," he repeated in a way that made it sound as if my name was wrapped in chocolate and would roll off his tongue.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Excuse me? That doesn't even make sense. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Stomach full of tiny lead balls, I turned left.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />1. Ew.<br />2. No. <br /><br /><br />And then there are the modern words casually thrown into a medieval-like fantasy world. <br /><br />1. Wow<br />2. Okay<br />3. "I totally got that"<br />4. "It was so not"<br />5. Basically<br />6. Hormones<br />7. Whatever<br /><br />I mean, seriously. Hormones?? <br /><br />There were more, but you're probably tired of this exquisitely horrible writing. <br /><br /><br />I've been procrastinating addressing the biggest problem of this book, so here it is. <br /><br /><b>Hawke.</b><br /><br />Everyone is surprised except for me. <br /><br />When Hawke first meets Poppy, he immediately nicknames her Princess, which is not only derogatory, it's also overused and the definition of cringe. But Poppy doesn't mind because HIS EYES ARE SPECIAL, DID I MENTION HIS SPECIAL EYES? THEY'RE GOLDEN. YEAH. SO THEY'RE SO SPECIAL AND SPARKLY AND-- Edward, anyone? <br /><br />Anyway, he's a stereotype who gives me MAJOR creep vibes. The creepometer is going wild with this one. We need to stop romanticizing predators. Sure, he's sOfT once you get to know him, but that does not mean he's a good person. I don't ship it. I ship Poppy with... maybe a rock? A therapy rock? <br /><br />This is not romantic at all. Hawke is a creepy, crusty guy with questionable morals, he's not even interesting, and Poppy Seed deserves better. AKA, her therapy rock. Even idiots deserve good partners, hm?<br /><br /><br />I made 5 new shelves specifically for this book: "idek-anymore-guys," "misplaced-hype," "new-level-of-trash," "i-am-disgusted," and "le-sigh." You're welcome.<br /><br /><br />(There goes the last of my faith in humanity and the Goodreads Choice Awards.) <br /><br />0.1 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="10941263401578012023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3256296986" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3256296986" />
    <a title="Jessica " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4844580-jessica"><img alt="Jessica " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494278516p2/4844580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3256296986?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica " href="/user/show/4844580-jessica">Jessica </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4844580-jessica?shelf=damaged-hero">damaged-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4844580-jessica?shelf=fantasy-romance">fantasy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4844580-jessica?shelf=forbidden-romance">forbidden-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4844580-jessica?shelf=favorite-of-2020">favorite-of-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3256296986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4952133001775012961">WHY DID I NOT LISTEN TO EVERYONE WHO TOLD ME HOW AMAZING THIS BOOK WAS!?!? I've had this book since March and have been putting off reading it because it's over 500 pages. But I finally picked it up for a vlog and it is easily one of my new favorite books of 2020. <br/><br/>Poppy is a Maiden and is following orders and waiting for until the time for her Ascension. That means that she stays in her room, cannot show her face to anyone, cannot be friends with anyone, and must follow the orders of the Duke an</span>
  <span id="freeText4952133001775012961" style="display:none">WHY DID I NOT LISTEN TO EVERYONE WHO TOLD ME HOW AMAZING THIS BOOK WAS!?!? I've had this book since March and have been putting off reading it because it's over 500 pages. But I finally picked it up for a vlog and it is easily one of my new favorite books of 2020. <br /><br />Poppy is a Maiden and is following orders and waiting for until the time for her Ascension. That means that she stays in her room, cannot show her face to anyone, cannot be friends with anyone, and must follow the orders of the Duke and the Duchess. But one night she decides to sneaks out to live a little and has an unforgettable encounter with a Royal Guard named Hawke. Soon, Hawke is actually replacing one of her personal guards and Poppy finds herself around Hawke all the time. With her feelings and attraction becoming harder to ignore, Poppy begins uncovering secrets about the kingdom and her duties while falling for her mysterious and enticing guard. <br /><br />THIS ROMANCE. GAHHH. Okay, so the beginning of this book is slow. Poppy and Hawke have a moment in the very beginning and then nothing really happens between them for another 200 pages. But once we reach 200 pages, this book does not slow down until the very last page. I was obsessed with the chemistry between Hawke and Poppy and by the end, I was literally obsessed with Hawke. I love how he knows Poppy has trained her whole life to protect herself and trusts her to take care of herself while fighting is going on. The entire dynamic between Hawke and Poppy was to die for and I could not get enough. <br /><br />The twists and turns in this book really got to me and I never saw them coming until literally the page before things were revealed. I am so happy that my sister had already read this because I was running to her every twenty pages to freak out over something new. AND THAT ENDING. I am so relieved that I only have to wait until September to get book two because I NEEEED to figure out what happens next. <br /><br />If you're like me and waited to pick up this book, STOP EVERYTHING AND READ IT NOW. I definitely think that fans of the ACOTAR series will love this book and you're going to fall in love with Hawke. Is it September yet? </span>
  <a data-text-id="4952133001775012961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
