<div id="review_3254837607" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3254837607" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3254837607?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781952457128" href="/book/show/55512450-from-blood-and-ash">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=best-of-2020">best-of-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3254837607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3288969421844315139"><i>“Fear and bravery are often one and the same. It either makes you a warrior or a coward. The only difference is the person it resides inside.”</i><br/><br/>For the record, this is my <i>NINETEENTH</i> Jennifer L. Armentrout novel that I've read and <b>my favourite</b>, thus far!!! (Do I say that with every book of hers I read? Yes, but that doesn’t make it any less true <3) If you had asked me 24 hours ago what my favourite JLA series was, I’d have immediately answered with the <i>Covenant</i> series because <b>hello! greek mytholog</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3288969421844315139" style="display:none"><i>“Fear and bravery are often one and the same. It either makes you a warrior or a coward. The only difference is the person it resides inside.”</i><br><br>For the record, this is my <i>NINETEENTH</i> Jennifer L. Armentrout novel that I've read and <b>my favourite</b>, thus far!!! (Do I say that with every book of hers I read? Yes, but that doesn’t make it any less true &lt;3) If you had asked me 24 hours ago what my favourite JLA series was, I’d have immediately answered with the <i>Covenant</i> series because <b>hello! greek mythology!!!</b> But, having read this…and despite it being her first venture into true high fantasy…this is also JLA’s <b>best-written series</b> yet, in my opinion. <br><br>Is it the best of the best in terms of <i>world building</i> (there isn’t even a map included in this book, but there is in the next instalment, so don’t worry :P) and <i>character development</i>? No, I’ve definitely read better, but it has such an <b>addictive quality</b> to it, which makes it such a <b>fun and enjoyable</b> read!!! (Thank you for saving me from my <i>book slump</i> – yet again, JLA ;)) <br><br>I know I <i>couldn’t put it down</i> last night and flew through it, while screaming to my friend at the top of my lungs <b>at 4am</b> about how much <b>I love</b> this book. And by the way, most of my texts looked like this: “<i>ASHSDFHKUFDGHKFDHFDSHKDGFHJKGDFHJKDFGHJKGDHJK !!!</i>” You’re welcome, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3344740393" rel="nofollow noopener">Alison</a> xD <br><br><i>“You're an absolutely stunning, murderous little creature.”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1601672763ra/30185995.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This story revolves around <b>Poppy</b>, who was raised to be the <i>Maiden</i>, forced to live a life of <i>solitude and isolation</i>, not even permitted to be looked at or spoken to either. Stuck seeing the world from behind a veil, she is considered as a holy figure who was chosen to become Ascended, the highest of honours in this society, and she is expected to feel thankful, rather than suffocated…but she doesn’t. <br><br><i>“With my sword and with my life, I vow to keep you safe, Penellaphe,” he spoke, voice deep and smooth, reminding me of rich, decadent chocolate. “From this moment until the last moment, I am yours.”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1601672763ra/30185994.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then, in walks <b>Hawke</b> into her life. He becomes her new <i>personal guard</i>, duty-bound to protect her, yet also undeniably attracted to her, which prompts the two of them beginning this <i>passionate and witty dance</i>. Blurring the lines between duty and desire, Poppy wants to abandon what’s always been expected of her and to chase after what she wants for the first time in her life. <br><br>So many aspects of this novel appealed to me <b>so much</b>. <i>The banter. The humour. The smut. The romance. The guard/royalty trope. The lust. The slow burn. The supernatural elements. The political intrigue. The mythology.</i> It really seemed like JLA wrote this with everything that I enjoy in mind. <br><br>This also really seemed like <b>Jude and Cardan</b> from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26032825.The_Cruel_Prince__The_Folk_of_the_Air___1_" title="The Cruel Prince (The Folk of the Air, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cruel Prince</a> were combined with <b>Yelena and Valek</b> from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60510.Poison_Study__Study___1_" title="Poison Study (Study, #1) by Maria V. Snyder" rel="nofollow noopener">Poison Study</a>, as well as <b>Lara and Aren</b> from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43383182.The_Bridge_Kingdom__The_Bridge_Kingdom___1_" title="The Bridge Kingdom (The Bridge Kingdom, #1) by Danielle L. Jensen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bridge Kingdom</a>. Hawke’s complete <i>acceptance and adoration</i> of Poppy’s ability to handle herself reminded me so much of how Cardan treated Jude. They both loved these women, flaws and all, and completely embraced their <b>violent tendencies</b>, hehe. In terms of <i>Poison Study</i>, I was happy to see some political intrigue and a more mature relationship, despite it being considered an inappropriate one, since both Hawke and Valek were guards. And then, of course, the more mature content (<i>profanity and smut</i>) and high fantasy setting also reminded me of <i>The Bridge Kingdom</i>. <br><br>But this book was also unique enough, with its own <b>original mythology</b> (although it did seem heavily influenced by <i>Greco-Roman mythology</i>, which I didn’t mind at all!!! :D) and a new take on <b>paranormal creatures</b> – such as <i>vampires and werewolves</i>, that it feels <b>fresh and innovative</b>, as well. JLA has successfully created something entirely her own, which stands her apart from the plethora of high fantasy out there. I loved this <i>so, so much</i>. If I could give it <b>100 stars</b> for pure enjoyment, I would. <br><br>By the way, if you wanted a <i>master-list</i> of all the gods to keep track of, here you go: <br>- <b>Nyktos</b>: the King of the Gods<br>- <b>Rhahar</b>: the Eternal God<br>- <b>Ione</b>: the Goddess of Rebirth<br>- <b>Aios</b>: the Goddess of Love, Fertility, and Beauty<br>- <b>Saion</b>: the God of the Sky and Soil<br>- <b>Theon</b>: the God of Accord and War<br>- <b>Lailah</b>: the Goddess of Peace and Vengeance<br>- <b>Bele</b>: the Goddess of the Hunt<br>- <b>Perus</b>: the God of Rite and Prosperity<br>- <b>Rhain</b>: the God of the Common Man and Endings<br>- <b>Penellaphe</b>: the Goddess of Wisdom, Loyalty, and Duty<br><br>Hopefully, with the popularity and fandoms that exist for <i>The Bridge Kingdom</i> and <i>From Blood and Ash</i>, this will be the beginning of a new era where <b>New Adult fantasy</b> will get the <i>recognition it deserves</i> as a genre by publishers, due to how many of us YA readers find ourselves <b>ageing out</b> of the genre. I, for one, want more books like these, where I can see people my age, living out stories that <i>I’d like to be a part of</i>. <br><br>I <b>highly, highly recommend</b> this series, as well as the other ones I’ve mentioned throughout this review. Now, I’m off to pick up the <i>recently released</i> sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/54319549.A_Kingdom_of_Flesh_and_Fire__Blood_and_Ash___2_" title="A Kingdom of Flesh and Fire (Blood and Ash, #2) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">A Kingdom of Flesh and Fire</a>, <b>yay</b>! :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="3288969421844315139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14316641651219354363"><a href='https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/><b>DNF @ 13%</b><br/><br/><br/><br/>I'm honestly flummoxed by the ratings of this book. How can <a href='https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/2020/10/damsel-by-elana-k-arnold.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>DAMSEL</a>, one of the best YA fantasies I've read recently, have a 3.4 rating on Goodreads, and this self-indulgent vampire AU version of ACoTaR has a 4.4? Like... I literally have no words. This is why I have trust issues, you guys. You have led me astray from the path of light.<br/><br/><br/><br/>FROM BLOOD AND ASH was all over my feed and even though I haven't been impressed with Armentrou</span>
  <span id="freeText14316641651219354363" style="display:none"><a href="https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br><b>DNF @ 13%</b><br><br><br><br>I'm honestly flummoxed by the ratings of this book. How can <a href="https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/2020/10/damsel-by-elana-k-arnold.html" rel="nofollow noopener">DAMSEL</a>, one of the best YA fantasies I've read recently, have a 3.4 rating on Goodreads, and this self-indulgent vampire AU version of ACoTaR has a 4.4? Like... I literally have no words. This is why I have trust issues, you guys. You have led me astray from the path of light.<br><br><br><br>FROM BLOOD AND ASH was all over my feed and even though I haven't been impressed with Armentrout's previous works (all of her heroines are basically the same person with different hair), I am a sucker for vampires and court intrigue, and so I thought to myself, "You know, maybe this could be awesome." Famous last words, I know. You'd think I'd learn my lesson by now, and stop reading books just because "all my friends are doing it," and yet here we are. I've been impressed by authors before, whose works I didn't like in the beginning and then they did a total 360, like they missed the freeway off-ramp to the Town of Awesome by complete accident and all it took was a U-turn.<br><br><br><br>But no. this was... bad. It's one of those "historical" fantasy worlds, but the heroine talks like it's modern day whatever. The love interest is a smirky smarmosaur who immediately starts calling the heroine "princess." She's a virgin because "reasons," which... okay. The whole beginning of the book is just a slew of info-dumping and I can already tell I'm going to despise the heroine. And the hero. And probably everyone else in this book.<br><br><br><br>1 star</span>

  <span id="freeText147664313842212171" style="display:none">After a long pause from reading, and a need for an escape from Sarah J Maas over descriptive writing, I came for this book... only to get traumatized even more!!! It was beyond horrible, the writing consists of too much info dumps and blabbering that I just wanted to scream at the main character to SHUT THE F*** UP!!! God! I dunno how I managed to last till 40%. And I hated the modern language but what’s worse is that some sentences are so grammatically incorrect your mind just gets a brainshock every now and then as you read on. The romance, it does not even deserve to be called romance, is cringe AF. So happy I managed to ask for a refund after this disaster. Too bad I can’t get my time back. I’m so gonna look for your reviews before I start reading from now on, you seem to have a similar annoyance scale to mine 😂 Now I’m gonna go and try to heal myself with something good, and by that I mean I’m gonna grab myself a Damsel.</span>

<div id="review_3353660398" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3353660398" />
    <a title="Lucie V." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84801697-lucie-v"><img alt="Lucie V." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597788485p2/84801697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3353660398?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucie V." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucie V." href="/user/show/84801697-lucie-v">Lucie V.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/52941854-from-blood-and-ash">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84801697-lucie-v?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84801697-lucie-v?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3353660398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8007766889943111450">Oh. My. God. One of the best book I've read.<br/>So much drama, so much angst, so worth it.<br/><br/>The beginning is a little slow (the first 10% maybe), but get ready because the rest is <b>AMAZING</b>. This book is addictive even though the pace is slow for most of the book. The world-building is great, even if some things may be a little confusing at first, and I just loved the two main characters.<br/><br/>Poppy was bland in the first few chapters, but she showed soon enough that she is not the boring and tame Maiden that</span>
  <span id="freeText8007766889943111450" style="display:none">Oh. My. God. One of the best book I've read.<br />So much drama, so much angst, so worth it.<br /><br />The beginning is a little slow (the first 10% maybe), but get ready because the rest is <b>AMAZING</b>. This book is addictive even though the pace is slow for most of the book. The world-building is great, even if some things may be a little confusing at first, and I just loved the two main characters.<br /><br />Poppy was bland in the first few chapters, but she showed soon enough that she is not the boring and tame Maiden that she was raised to be. She is not feeling thankful as she should be. She wants adventure, she wants to help her people and mostly, she wants to live. As the Maiden, she can't interact with anyone except her two personal guards, her lady in waiting, and the Duke and Duchess who are taking care of her (taking care might not be the adequate word when talking about the Duke, but I digress...). Poppy must always wear a veil that covers her hair and the top half of her face and no one ever questioned it, until her new guard, the gorgeous Hawke Flynn, comes into the story and starts treating her as a human being and not just as a religious symbol.<br /><br />Hawke is an amazing character, his relationship with Poppy reminds me a little of Jude and Cardan in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26032825.The_Cruel_Prince__The_Folk_of_the_Air___1_" title="The Cruel Prince (The Folk of the Air, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cruel Prince</a>, the mix of banter and sexual tension was a delight to read. Near the end of the book, they reminded me of Feyre and Rhysand at the beginning of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17927395.A_Court_of_Mist_and_Fury__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___2_" title="A Court of Mist and Fury (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #2) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Mist and Fury</a> which is perfect because I just <b>love</b> them and I hope Poppy and Hawke's relationship <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(or I should say Poppy and Casteel's relationship) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> will continue to have some drama and love-hate in the next book (I need a regular dose of love-hate and angst).<br /><br />The mix of a fantasy setting with the Greco-roman inspired gods and the new (and innovative) way to present vampires and werewolves gave an awesome result. Even though nothing in this book is really new (individually), the way the author took all these pieces and mixed them together to create something new. <br /><br />I honestly don't have the words to explain how great this book is. I think my brain and my heart are still reeling from the rollercoaster of emotions in the last 20% of the book. Even though From Blood and Ash is over 600 pages I read it in two days and it went by so fast. It is a good thing that I already have the second book, I don't know how I would have been able to wait for a whole year before reading it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8007766889943111450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3532762367" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3532762367" />
    <a title="preoccupiedbybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36310974-preoccupiedbybooks"><img alt="preoccupiedbybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577647566p2/36310974.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3532762367?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="preoccupiedbybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="preoccupiedbybooks" href="/user/show/36310974-preoccupiedbybooks">preoccupiedbybooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3532762367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8916177944581564397">3.5 stars 🗡️🗡️🗡️ 1/2<br/><br/><b>An addictive and fun romantic NA fantasy featuring romance, friendship, betrayal, violence, vengeance and loneliness!</b><br/><br/><i>Poppy is the Maiden, the chosen one, never to be looked at, touched or spoken to. She lives a solitary and lonely life waiting to be given to the Gods at her Ascension. But Poppy would prefer to be fighting the evil which killed her parents, or sneaking out at night, and she secretly dreads her Ascension. Her kingdom depends on her, but Poppy is more than the M</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8916177944581564397" style="display:none">3.5 stars 🗡️🗡️🗡️ 1/2<br><br><b>An addictive and fun romantic NA fantasy featuring romance, friendship, betrayal, violence, vengeance and loneliness!</b><br><br><i>Poppy is the Maiden, the chosen one, never to be looked at, touched or spoken to. She lives a solitary and lonely life waiting to be given to the Gods at her Ascension. But Poppy would prefer to be fighting the evil which killed her parents, or sneaking out at night, and she secretly dreads her Ascension. Her kingdom depends on her, but Poppy is more than the Maiden, she wants more! When Poppy gets a new guard, Hawke, she finds herself drawn to him, challenged by him and tempted by him. Poppy not only risks her heart, but her life, and soon everything is turned upside down and starts falling apart!</i><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52831200.From_Blood_and_Ash__Blood_and_Ash___1_" title="From Blood and Ash (Blood and Ash, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">From Blood and Ash</a> was a super quick and fun buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/22314328" rel="nofollow noopener">Aoife</a>, and I really enjoyed discussing the twists and reveals, our predictions, thoughts and feelings! It was also my first <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4476934.Jennifer_L__Armentrout" title="Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer L. Armentrout</a> book, after being a bit confused and scared of all of her interconnecting series!<br><br>I will start with the good stuff! This story had kings, queens, creatures, magical forests, a dark history and lots and lots of secrets!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497683302ra/23048872.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It had some great action scenes, and I could really visualise being there in amongst all the violence! Seriously, I got GOT vibes from some of the bloodthirsty scenes! There was angst, banter, an interesting plot, and a brave, sassy badass female lead, who was just discovering herself. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52831200.From_Blood_and_Ash__Blood_and_Ash___1_" title="From Blood and Ash (Blood and Ash, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">From Blood and Ash</a> was a fast paced page turner, and I couldn't stop reading it! I was meant to read five chapters a day, but poor Aoife had to put up with me 'accidentally' skipping ahead a few times, when I couldn't bring myself to stop reading!<br>Entertaining, and full of tropes, FBAA was very romance heavy, and the two main characters had sizzling chemistry. This was no YA fantasy, with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4476934.Jennifer_L__Armentrout" title="Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer L. Armentrout</a> writing some steamy scenes for her readers! That girl can certainly write a sex scene ha ha!<br>🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥🔥<br><br>Having said that, I did have some issues! Firstly the plot was predictable as fuck! The foreshadowing was way too heavy, and we pretty much called every twist from the first few chapters. I've seen other readers say that they could see what was going to happen, but that didn't stop them from loving it, but sadly, I was really disappointed that everything played out how we thought it would! Looking back at our text chain, it was clear that Aoife and I tried to convince ourselves that we were wrong about our predictions, and tried to throw out other options, but nope we nailed every plot twist, from the little things, to the major ones. I'd like to say that we're amazing detectives, but unfortunately, I think it was just that blatant! Poppy just wasn't very smart...there were some really obvious shit, that she just didn't pick up on, and it was frustrating!<br><br>The writing style was fairly simple for a so called high fantasy book, and it really reminded me of ACOTAR by SJM and even Twilight a little bit! They had the same addictive quality which makes readers devour their books, but actually the writing isn't really that good?! The more I think about it actually, the more Hawke seems a tiny bit like someone else we might know, whose name rhymes with fleece....in every single way! *whistles*<br><br>The ending...what a clusterfuck that was! After all Poppy had been through in her life, having no voice or choice in her own life, to be treated like that was appalling! I sincerely hope that she stands up for herself and that he doesn't get his own way. Then there was the build up to the ending where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[they have sex, even though Poppy has just found out he is the enemy, has been betrayed and she has stabbed him?! WTF?!<br><br>Actually the more I think about how P and H met, after finding out the truth, the more disturbed and creeped out I feel.<br><br>The fangs? How did none of them notice them, especially the girl kissing and having sex with him?!<br>Then there is the 200 year old taking the 18 year old's virginity.. ick <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>So nope I'm not 100% sold on the romance at the moment, but I liked the world it was set in, even if it wasn't that original, and I am curious about the Capital and about a certain other place! I did like some of the side characters. Tawny and Viktor were gorgeous, and Kieran was more intriguing to Aoife and I than Hawke lol! I wold definitely like to find out more about him, and his background!<br><br>I am definitely not the target audience for this series, but despite it's faults, I can't deny that I devoured it, and had a lot of fun?! So sign me up for the recently released <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/54319549.A_Kingdom_of_Flesh_and_Fire__Blood_and_Ash___2_" title="A Kingdom of Flesh and Fire (Blood and Ash, #2) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">A Kingdom of Flesh and Fire</a>, especially after seeing people react strongly to the ending?!! Hopefully, that one will be less predictable, and will surprise me, yet still stay as entertaining as this one. Maybe certain characters will grow on me, and I really hope there will still be deliciously violent action scenes!<br>Thanks for the buddy read Aoife, we can now start the next one 😂 </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8916177944581564397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3511596434" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3511596434" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8429172-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595453256p2/8429172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3511596434?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/8429172-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=ebooks-i-own">ebooks-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=reading-slowly">reading-slowly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=jlarmentrout-books">jlarmentrout-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3511596434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14200089157673512664">My level of enjoyment was off the charts with this book.<br/><br/>It had been around 4 years since the last time I picked up anything by this author and I'm happy to see this story is not like her previous work. Yes, there were elements here and there that reminded me a bit of The Covenant series but I liked how all the characters had their own voice (something she used to struggle with in the past) and they're not recycled.<br/><br/>This book felt like coming back home after a long journey and it was fun. There we</span>
  <span id="freeText14200089157673512664" style="display:none">My level of enjoyment was off the charts with this book.<br /><br />It had been around 4 years since the last time I picked up anything by this author and I'm happy to see this story is not like her previous work. Yes, there were elements here and there that reminded me a bit of The Covenant series but I liked how all the characters had their own voice (something she used to struggle with in the past) and they're not recycled.<br /><br />This book felt like coming back home after a long journey and it was fun. There were your typical tropes but with a spin so they felt fresh and I don't have any complaints.<br /><br />The pacing was fine, I liked all the characters, I liked the romance, the history... I really liked this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14200089157673512664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4810984050146984534" style="display:none"><u>Star Rating</u>: <i>—&gt;</i> <b>5 Stars</b><br /><br />OHMYGODDDD. This was f*cking fantastic. This was just SO. GOOD. <br /><br /><b>GOLD, PURE <i>GOLD</i></b><br /><br />i can’t even take the feelings that I have... going on... right now.<br /><br />This was absolutely intoxicating. Every second. And omfg so swoon worthy. <br /><br />I loved how I truly felt, on some level, a connection with Poppy, where I was finding things out in time, just as she was. I really liked this. It was refreshing to be constantly guessing! Some of the outcome was predictable, but only to a certain degree, and the rest was definitely not was I was expecting. Honestly, though, I had no idea what to expect, so. 🤷🏼‍♀️<br /><br />What I got though, was a richly imagined Paranormal Romance in a high fantasy world with incredible characters. I might’ve even cried in several moments. Felt joy, frustration, anger, <i>fire</i>... I felt like everything Poppy felt, I could feel. And God is she a BADASS! She don’t take no sh*t!!<br /><br />I just love JLA SO much. <br />She writes in a way that is just so. damn. compelling! She has never disappointed me before, and she beyond exceeded expectations this time. <br />I don’t know how long I’m going to have to wait for Blood &amp; Ash #2... but I NEED IT NOW!!!! <br /><br />The ending hints of what is to come, and I have ideas, because, no way was that ending 100% serious! But yeah. Holy sh*t. I am SO looking forward to the journey in the next book &amp; seeing where poppy goes from here. I truly love her as our MC. She’s just <i>FAB</i> !<br /><br />100% recommend.<br /><br />Truly the greatest surprise ever. What a book! Whew! <br />Jennifer L. Armentrout you have my thanks, gratitude, &amp; heart. 😂<br /><br />❤️🖤♥️🖤❤️<br /><br /><br />_____________________<br />So damn thankful for this freakin’ surprise of a novel from one of my fav authors; saved me from a book slump!<br /> <br />_____________________<br />Omfg where did this even come from?!?!?</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11518665700006081109"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590848002ra/29566227.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i> I was the Maiden, the Chosen … I wasn’t Poppy but a shadow of a person who wasn’t allowed to experience, need, live, or want.</i><br/><br/>Story 🌟🌟🌟🌟<br/>Poppy always knew that as a Maiden she needed to follow the rules. <br/>Be pure, innocent. <br/>The perfect Maiden. <br/>But even though she understood her role in the world, she didn’t obey completely.<br/>One day her rebellious side brings her into a room with a handsome dangerous man. <br/>Being absolutely alone with him and hidden through a mask. <br/>No one would know that she kissed a </span>
  <span id="freeText11518665700006081109" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590848002ra/29566227.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> I was the Maiden, the Chosen … I wasn’t Poppy but a shadow of a person who wasn’t allowed to experience, need, live, or want.</i><br><br>Story 🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>Poppy always knew that as a Maiden she needed to follow the rules. <br>Be pure, innocent. <br>The perfect Maiden. <br>But even though she understood her role in the world, she didn’t obey completely.<br>One day her rebellious side brings her into a room with a handsome dangerous man. <br>Being absolutely alone with him and hidden through a mask. <br>No one would know that she kissed a man even though she shouldn’t. <br>But still chaos breaks out and Poppy learns that she didn’t know what living means until she met this man. <br><br>Even though I kind of knew what was going to be the “big” plot twist I still enjoyed the story immensely. I loved that the author gave us crumps of hidden parts where we could’ve figured things out. <br>And even though this one wasn’t that surprising, the end still had some surprises for me and I loved it! <br>That was so addictive! I missed books like this and I can’t wait to read the second book.<br>GIMME! 😭😭😭<br><br>Characters 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br><br><i> “You're an absolutely stunning, murderous little creature.” </i><br><br>I haven’t read about such a fierce strong female character in a long time. <br>I fell in love with Poppy in just a few pages. <br>She was extremely skilled with weapons, knew how to defend herself and was loyal to the people she loved and cared about. <br>She let herself be treated horribly, just so her loved ones weren’t in danger. <br>But she was never completely obedient. <br>She rebelled all the time. <br>She snuck out, she fought, she read books that were forbidden for her. <br>She was brave, when others trembled. <br>Ugh, I’m in love. <br>And Hawke... I wasn’t so sure in the beginning, but halfway through the book I fell in love with him too. He was such a charming, respectful and supportive man. <br>He didn’t treat Poppy as If she was the maiden. He treated her with dignity, respect, he knew that she could defend herself, but still helped or saved her, when he knew she needed his help. <br>He was such a gentleman, but still had a naughty side. He was joking, making filthy comments and driving Poppy crazy. <br>I loved them both so much. <br><br>The side characters, like Vikter etc. we’re also written in a great way that pushed the story forward. <br><br>World 🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>Most of the book I was doubting myself and my knowledge of the English language. <br>I was so confused most of the time and thought that maybe I just didn’t get all the words. But that wasn’t true, because after reading the full book I get the whole world building. And it is so cool! <br>It is a mixture of vampires, werewolves and other monsters. <br>The most interesting magical thing was definitely Poppy with her abilities to feel the emotions of others and partly controlling or shifting them. <br>I can’t wait to read more of the world, because after finishing and understanding it, <br>I am now even more curious! <br><br>Relationships 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br><br><i> “I’m the Maiden, Hawke,” <br>I reminded him – or myself, I wasn’t sure.<br>“And I don’t care.”<br>My eyes flew open in shock. <br>“I can’t believe you just said that.”<br>“I did. And I’ll say it again. I don’t care what you are.” Hawke’s hand slid off my back. <br>A moment later, I felt his palm flatten against my cheek with unerring accuracy. <br>“I care about who you are.”</i><br><br>I lived for the romance in this book. <br>They had such an amazing relationship. <br>Poppy and Hawke were extremely attracted to each other. One thing I absolutely adored was their flirty banter. <br>The sexual tension was enorm. <br>Next to being funny and flirty, they respected and cared for each other. <br>He supported her to stand on her own two feet and choose her own path. <br>He knew her abilities and didn’t try to dim it. <br>They fell in love with each other and I loved it. <br>I couldn’t stop reading because of it. <br>It was so addictive! <br><br>Writing style 🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>That was my first Armentrout book, but now I know why she is so popular. It was written in a perfect pacing and the flirting between those two always made me laugh. <br>I was addicted not only to the story, but also to the writing which was flowing and pushing the plot forward. <br>I enjoyed it so much and can’t wait for the second book! <br><br><i> Death is like an old friend who pays a visit, sometimes when it’s least expected and other times when you’re waiting for her. <br>It’s neither the first nor the last time she’ll pay a visit, but that doesn’t make any death less harsh or unforgiving.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11518665700006081109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3361494055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9831374388591907689"><a href='http://caitsbooks.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Check out this review (and more) over on my blog!</a><br/><br/><b>Quick Stats:<br/>Overall:</b>5/5 Stars<br/><b>Characters:</b> 5/5<br/><b>Setting:</b> 5/5<br/><b>Writing:</b> 5/5<br/><b>Plot and Themes:</b> 5/5<br/><b>Awesomeness Factor:</b> 4.5/5<br/><b>Review in a Nutshell: </b><i>From Blood and Ash</i> was incredible. From the romance to the world, I was captivated. Excuse me as I count down the days until the sequel.<br/><br/><br/><i>“Fear and bravery are often one and the same. It either makes you a warrior or a coward. The only difference is the person it resides inside.”</i><br/><br/><i>// Content Warning: Violence, Death, A</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9831374388591907689" style="display:none"><a href="http://caitsbooks.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Check out this review (and more) over on my blog!</a><br /><br /><b>Quick Stats:<br />Overall:</b>5/5 Stars<br /><b>Characters:</b> 5/5<br /><b>Setting:</b> 5/5<br /><b>Writing:</b> 5/5<br /><b>Plot and Themes:</b> 5/5<br /><b>Awesomeness Factor:</b> 4.5/5<br /><b>Review in a Nutshell: </b><i>From Blood and Ash</i> was incredible. From the romance to the world, I was captivated. Excuse me as I count down the days until the sequel.<br /><br /><br /><i>“Fear and bravery are often one and the same. It either makes you a warrior or a coward. The only difference is the person it resides inside.”</i><br /><br /><i>// Content Warning: Violence, Death, Assault, Mature Content, Suicide Mention, Abuse, Animal Death, Murder, Kidnapping/Abduction //</i><br /><br /><i>“Some truths do nothing but destroy and decay what they do not obliterate. Truths do not always set one free. Only a fool who has spent their entire life being fed lies believes that.”</i><br /><br /><b>Release Date:</b> 3/30/2020<br /><b>Publisher:</b> Blue Box Press<br /><b>Page Count:</b> 634<br /><b>Premise:</b><br /><br /><i>From Blood and Ash</i> follows Poppy, who was chosen to be the Maiden. The Maiden must live a solitary life until she is given to the gods at her Ascension, a fate Poppy dreads, despite it being the highest honor. When she gets a new guard, the attractive and alluring Hawke, Poppy finds herself drawn to him, despite knowing that it could make the gods deem her unworthy. But with a fallen kingdom on the rise, she not only has to worry about losing the gods’ approval, but also her life.<br /><br /><i>“‘You're such a bad influence.’<br />‘Only the bad can be influenced, Princess.’”</i><br /><br /><b>- Writing &amp; Setting -</b> <br /><br />Jennifer L. Armentrout’s writing is perfect for this book. It’s easy to read and understand, yet can fit the atmosphere of the world she’s created. Speaking of the world, it was not what I expected. There are slight nods to creatures we’re familiar with but they have unique twists that make them stand out. <br /><br /><i>“Lust was not love, it was not loyalty, and it was not long lasting.”</i><br /><br /><b>- Plot -</b><br /><br /><b>I was addicted to this book. The first 50 pages or so were a little slower as a lot of important information was dealt out, but the rest flew by</b>. I never wanted to put it down. There’s <b>plenty of action throughout the book, but it’s the romance that drives the plot</b> forward. <br /><br />There are also some<b> fantastic twists.</b> If you read a lot of fantasy novels, you might be able to predict the big twist like I did, but even though I had an idea about what was going to happen, I was still so excited and shocked when it did. <br /><br /><i>“You’re an absolutely stunning, murderous little creature.”</i><br /><br /><b>- Characters - </b><br /><br />The characters are where this book is the most fun. Mostly because of the romance but we’ll get to that in a second.<br /><br />Poppy is our protagonist, and<b> I loved how strong and caring she was</b>. Her empathy yet ruthlessness (so violent) was so interesting to watch. And then there’s Hawke. He’s just *chef’s kiss*. His banter with Poppy was so fun and I really can’t wait to learn even more about him in the sequel. We also had a lot of strong side characters that I loved.<br /><br />Okay but let’s talk about the romance for a second. <b>It was so perfect. It was swoon-worthy and angsty and absolutely addictive.</b> Also, be warned, this is definitely New Adult and <i>NOT</i> YA. <br /><br /><b>- Conclusion -</b><br /><br /><b>Pros-</b> amazing romance, interesting world, addictive, impossible to put down<br /><b>Cons- </b>slower start<br /><b>Overall- 5/5 stars. <br /><i>From Blood and Ash</i> is a book that you will get obsessed with. This book is so much more than I thought it would be, and I’m dying to see where it goes. Fans of Sarah J. Maas- please pick this up. Even if you hate Sarah J. Maas- PICK THIS UP!</b><br /><br /><b>Follow Me Here: <a href="http://caitsbooks.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog </a>||<a href="http://caitsbooks.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr </a>||<a href="http://instagram.com/caitsbooks/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bookstagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/cait_jacobs" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>||<a href="http://caitsbooks.com/category/review/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Reviews </a> </b></span>

<div id="review_3255488115" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3255488115" />
    <a title="Dark River" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/89153171-dark-river"><img alt="Dark River" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550279719p2/89153171.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3255488115?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dark River" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dark River" href="/user/show/89153171-dark-river">Dark River</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3255488115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14965239534980214995">If you liked ACOTAR (and I mean specifically ACOTAR, not ACOMAF. We all like ACOMAF, sit down, Karen), you might like From Blood and Ash because most of this book feels exactly the same. As in, it feels like a giant, drawn out, novel-long prologue that leads up to what I'm hoping will be the real story in book 2. But let's not get ahead of ourselves; that is spoiler territory and we'll talk about that later.<br/><br/>Some general stuff first: The writing was okay. Not great, not horrible, just okay. But w</span>
  <span id="freeText14965239534980214995" style="display:none">If you liked ACOTAR (and I mean specifically ACOTAR, not ACOMAF. We all like ACOMAF, sit down, Karen), you might like From Blood and Ash because most of this book feels exactly the same. As in, it feels like a giant, drawn out, novel-long prologue that leads up to what I'm hoping will be the real story in book 2. But let's not get ahead of ourselves; that is spoiler territory and we'll talk about that later.<br /><br />Some general stuff first: The writing was okay. Not great, not horrible, just okay. But what it needed was an editor to take out all the unnecessary "..."s and "!"s and other annoying crap like that. Honestly, during the first couple chapters I felt like I was reading fanfiction more so than a finished novel, but it does get better. Or you just get used to it. One of the two, I'm not sure. <br /><br />The world is interesting, however, being introduced to it felt a little too info-dumpy at first, and a little too drawn out later, without actually getting all that much information that truly sinks in. I have no idea if that makes sense, but that's how it felt like to me. Like a lot of white noise. It's all there but it feels kinda half-cooked. Like more time should have gone into developing it and more thought into how the reader is supposed to experience it. (Also boy, some of those names are so cringe, I died a little. Not just names for people, some of those were alright, but mostly places and species.)<br /><br />The same thing is true for the plot. It went in circles or nowhere for over half the book and that made it drag, even though it's by no means complicated. On the contrary, it felt overly formulaic sometimes, but was spiked with so. much. unnecessary. filler. OMG. Half this book is completely optional. And I hate that, because the couple more action filled scenes that we got (and no, I don't just mean the banging), were really, really fun. I wanted more of that. I wanted to love this book and the characters, but I couldn't. Not fully. <br />Actually, let's dive into our main characters for a bit. That however means that in <br /><br />3<br /><br />2<br /><br />1<br /><br /><b>IT'S SPOILER TIME</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<u>Poppy</u><br />(Please tell me I'm not the only one who didn't like that name btw. No offense if your name is Poppy, it just didn't fit this book imho @_@ Penellaphe..?? - fuck, how do you spell that? - wasn't much better though. Like, shit, I'm still not sure if I even pronounce that correctly and normally I'm a big fan of long and kinda wtf names. I mean Malachiasz is my baby, ok)<br /><br />I didn't really like Poppy from the start, unfortunately. She's too trope-y, even for my cliché loving ass. And she tells me more about her development than she actually shows me and I HATE that, I hate that so much. You can do better as an author. <br />She's bland, she's stupid and I couldn't connect with her at all for the majority of the story. Which is a shame, because we do get glimpses of a much more interesting Poppy here and there. That scene when she turned Lord Mazeen into minced meat? Holy shit, YES. I loved how she completely snapped in her grief. It felt real and I'm pretty sure I even cried some angry tears with her while reading that. <br />I'm assuming, or at least I am strongly hoping, this is because our girl is still suffering from "Feyre stuck in the Spring Court - Syndrome" and will undergo some actual development in the next book to make her more fleshed out. I mean, I'm aware she's been stuck in a golden cage her whole life and was pushed into a dumb, docile role by the people around her, so I'll excuse that, partially, because of the story. But it's not just that. <br /><br />She makes really, really dumb decisions, doesn't think things through, or if she does, conveniently, her thoughts lead her in the completely wrong direction. That would be fun if I as the reader would be mislead with her. Hell, it'd be great and make the twists ahead just oh so much better. But I wasn't. Because even only knowing the information Poppy herself has, since we're stuck inside her head, what's been going on around her has been super transparent very early on. And yet, she refuses to see it. Now that's just frustrating and poor story-telling imho. And it really takes the cake when a protagonist like her is being praised for their intelligence by other characters in the same sentence they say/do something extra stupid. This happens A LOT. Almost as if the author thinks that if she just tells us often enough through people in-universe that Poppy is smart, we'll somehow believe it. Nah-ah. <br /><br />Like damn. I get it sis, we all wanna see the best in the people we like, no matter if they actually deserve it or not. Really, I understand, that's a very normal, human thing. What I don't understand is being so blinded by the dick that you refuse to acknowledge what's going on around you even with multiple people plus your own subconscious spelling it the fuck out for you :') <br /><br />Which brings us to <br /><u>Hawke/Casteel/The Dark One</u> (Ugh, The Dark One though? *rolls eyes*) <br />I don't know if his role here was meant to be so obvious (to anyone but Poppy at least) but it kinda took away from my enjoyment of him throughout the story. Still, he has potential. Especially if he'd be an actual villain.<br />Don't get me wrong, I love the misunderstood <i>(not really so)</i> bad boy thing as much as the next thot, but I don't need another Rhysand. The one is enough. What I want is another Darkling, except one who actually ends up with the girl. But somehow, SOMEHOW, I don't think that's what we're being served here lol <br />Because the Acotar vibes are STRONG in this one, young Padawan. <br /><br />- Sexy, ambiguously tan, black-haired? Check<br />- Overpowered fighter from a legendary, nearly immortal but demonized species? Check<br />- The villain but not really the villain? Check<br />- Only wanted to protect and fight for his people and family the entire time uwu? Check<br />- Steals protagonist away to his magical, hidden home? Check<br />- Magical hidden home behind the mountains that no one even knows still exists and is protected by spells so no outsider can enter? Why don't you straight up call it Velaris?? - CHECK<br />- Has been a (blood) whore for exactly <b>50 years</b> to a shadyass Queen??? FUCKING CHECK lmao <br /><br />Should I go on? <br />Oof. Still, I might not want another Rhys, but damn, I'll take it because Cas at least is actually fun and I found myself wanting to know more about his background, his family and where he comes from. And about Kieran. Please more about Kieran. I latched onto that boy so fast.<br /><br />But can we also please take a moment, while we're visiting side character hell, to talk about Tawny? <br />What in the everloving fuck was JLA thinking exactly when she decided it would be a great idea to make one of the only POC in this story so far, a dark-skinned girl with black curly hair, Poppy Sue's meaningless servant?? Plus calling her TAWNY 👏 LYON 👏 to top it all off? You can't be serious. Not in the year of our dark lord, 2020. I'm honestly still a little speechless and for a long time now thought that surely I must have misread something here, but nope, nope, I did not.<br />The author probably thought she did well because Tawny is described as gorgeous and that seems to make it all good in white people logic - not the first example of this, just the most recent I've encountered. But it really, really doesn't. <br /><br /><br />So, in conclusion From Blood and Ash has been a bit of a disappointment for me. I'm still kinda looking forward to book 2. Surprisingly. I don't know if that's a good thing or if I'm just setting myself up for more disappointment, because I'm expecting a glow up from Poppy, character-wise, that might not actually happen. And because I'm expecting a better, faster-paced and more emotionally gripping plot that might never come. But that's where I stand right now.<br />I love vampires, I love werewolves and I wanna see where this is going. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There is potential here and for the time being I'm rating it 3 stars. Leaving room for more, as the story continues, however, my hopes remain on the lower side of things.<br /><br />PS.: And yes, the sex is pretty alright, so if you're willing to trudge through 70% uneventful nothingness to get to the 20% genuinely fun plot / action and 10% smut like me, go ahead.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14965239534980214995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3255240980" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3255240980" />
    <a title="Valliya Rennell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58882300-valliya-rennell"><img alt="Valliya Rennell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596694907p2/58882300.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3255240980?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valliya Rennell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valliya Rennell" href="/user/show/58882300-valliya-rennell">Valliya Rennell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=a-3-25-stars">a-3-25-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=c-novel">c-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=d-fantasy">d-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=d-romance">d-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=x-reviewed-books">x-reviewed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=b-new-adult">b-new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3255240980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15130505402839482729">3.25 stars<br/><br/>It has been a hot minute since I've read a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4476934.Jennifer_L__Armentrout' title='Jennifer L. Armentrout' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jennifer L. Armentrout</a> book. She is my hands down favorite author. <b>Although this was my most disappointing book that I have read from her yet, I do think that the sequel will be much much better and I genuinely cannot wait. </b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52831200.From_Blood_and_Ash__Blood_and_Ash___1_' title='From Blood and Ash (Blood and Ash, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout' rel='nofollow noopener'>From Blood and Ash</a> is Armentrout's first high fantasy novel that she has written. We follow Penellaphe, Poppy, the Maiden: a girl who must be kept secluded and pure before she is given to the girls on the day of her Ascensi</span>
  <span id="freeText15130505402839482729" style="display:none">3.25 stars<br><br>It has been a hot minute since I've read a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4476934.Jennifer_L__Armentrout" title="Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer L. Armentrout</a> book. She is my hands down favorite author. <b>Although this was my most disappointing book that I have read from her yet, I do think that the sequel will be much much better and I genuinely cannot wait. </b><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52831200.From_Blood_and_Ash__Blood_and_Ash___1_" title="From Blood and Ash (Blood and Ash, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">From Blood and Ash</a> is Armentrout's first high fantasy novel that she has written. We follow Penellaphe, Poppy, the Maiden: a girl who must be kept secluded and pure before she is given to the girls on the day of her Ascension in hopes that she will one day save the kingdom. As her guard kicks the bucket during a series of murders going on in the castle, Hawke, a dashing new guard from the capital, is chosen to fill the role. As the day of her Ascension nears and pressures around her rise, <b>Poppy must finally figure out what is more important to her: serving a system she knows nothing about or actually living for a while?</b><br><br>The best part of the novel, other than the steamy romance, was definitely the subtle exploration of a very dark theme. Throughout the story Poppy goes round in circles <b>trying to figure out who she wants to be. </b>No one wants to let her figure this out as she is the Maiden and must be kept 'pure' for the gods. This means no interactions, no friends, no lovers, no learning of basic skills. She sacrifices so much without realising it because she is brainwashed that she is serving a greater purpose and she will help move her society forward. She sacrifices herself for the people. Although at surface level, one might not even notice the commentary present, I think that it is actually a very important aspect. I find that a lot of people in society lose themselves in their jobs, egos, and honor. They are so drilled to keep working, that they never even realise that they aren't human anymore, but are just people filling a mould created for them by their bosses. <br><br><b>My greatest issue with this book is the tragic, terrible, horrendous world-building.</b> I know that this is JLA's first high fantasy so I am trying to be as light here as possible, but wow. I struggled so much through the first 30% of the book because I just couldn't wrap my head around the <b>huge info-dumps</b> that happen in the beginning. Best part is, the info-dumps don't even explain half of the things that will be relevant moving forwards. Or they say one thing in passing and we are expected to remember it 200 pages down the road when it becomes relevant. After you wrap your head around what is going on, you'll be fine. The trouble is trying to understand the systems of the world in place.<br><br>As always, the <b>romance was great.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486484179ra/21919377.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Filled with angst and very steamy, sexy scenes, this book once again solidifies JLA in the pantheon of erotica/romance gods. I am just wowed. Although I did have a few problems with the love-interest, I found the relationship, the build up, and the pay off to be very well done. I genuinely cannot wait to see where things go from here.<br><br>In comparison to some of her other books, <b>the characterisation wasn't that great</b>. A lot of the characters were just shallow, for example, evil for the sake of being evil. There are literally two characters who do nothing in the story other than torture Poppy both mentally and physically... for NO REASON. If there was a reason for their actions, I guess I'd be fine with it(?). Even if the explanation would be that they get gratification through hurting others. We didn't get anything, though. I had issues with Hawke, the love interest. He reminded me of Rhysand from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_" title="A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Thorns and Roses</a> when he does kind of act like a sexual predator in book 1... but worse. I understand that most of the time Hawke toys with Poppy, but you get to a point where "no means no". I think that St. Delphi from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9680718.Half_Blood__Covenant___1_" title="Half-Blood (Covenant, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Half-Blood</a> is a perfect love interest. There were plenty sexy scenes there, but nothing JLA wrote ever went into that 'lowkey not ok' territory. <b>The two characters that I can whole-heartedly say that I really enjoyed were Poppy and her father figure Vikter.</b> Not only do I think that their relationship was well done, but I think that them by themselves seemed like real people. Both of them had motivations, unique perspectives that really shown through. Unfortunately, most of the other characters weren't that well done which caused a lot of <b>wonky dialogue</b><br><br>This book is <b>super atmospheric</b>. I loved how you could just sense the eeriness of the castle or the mystery of the Blood Forest. I thought this atmosphere that was present throughout gave the opportunity for the vampire-esque creatures to really get a unique feel and not be just another rip off of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a>. This atmospheric writing was something that I really haven't seen from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4476934.Jennifer_L__Armentrout" title="Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer L. Armentrout</a> before, however I think that if she really weighs into this for the sequel, it will be even better.<br><br>To quickly sum up, although <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52831200.From_Blood_and_Ash__Blood_and_Ash___1_" title="From Blood and Ash (Blood and Ash, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">From Blood and Ash</a> wasn't exactly my favorite book from my queen <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4476934.Jennifer_L__Armentrout" title="Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer L. Armentrout</a>, it was still a solid book that many people will enjoy much much more than I did. <b>I truly do recommend it to people. </b>Now that I finally understand the world and what is going on, I have <b>high hopes for the sequel!</b><br><br>----------------------<br><u>Blood and Ash</u>:<br>#1 From Blood and Ash: ★★★.25<br>#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3456537112" rel="nofollow noopener">A Kingdom of Flesh and Fire</a>: ★★★.25</span>
  <a data-text-id="15130505402839482729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AJ" href="/user/show/92947191-aj">AJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781952457005" href="/book/show/52861201-from-blood-and-ash">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92947191-aj?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3258022007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16738451510023535354"><b>
  <i>”Both halves are as beautiful as the whole."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Well ladies and gentleman, I present to you the best book I’ve read so far in 2020! I can’t believe how amazing, and sexy this book was! <br/><br/>The world building? Amazing!! The characters? Amazing! Creative and interesting powers, magic and backstory? Absolutely! This book had me hooked literally from the very first chapter. The concept of the <i>Maiden</i> and Poppy’s gifts were something I want to read more about. It’s been a while since I’ve read a book with</span>
  <span id="freeText16738451510023535354" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>”Both halves are as beautiful as the whole."</i>
</b><br /><br />Well ladies and gentleman, I present to you the best book I’ve read so far in 2020! I can’t believe how amazing, and sexy this book was! <br /><br />The world building? Amazing!! The characters? Amazing! Creative and interesting powers, magic and backstory? Absolutely! This book had me hooked literally from the very first chapter. The concept of the <i>Maiden</i> and Poppy’s gifts were something I want to read more about. It’s been a while since I’ve read a book with such unique magic!!<br /><br />I know a lot of people aren’t into smut or explicit scenes in books but if you’re like me, a slut for smut haha then you’ll be very happy with how well written the scenes are in this book. They were realistic, non cringy and H O T! I couldn’t get enough. With that being said, this book is <b>NOT</b> YA. <br /><br />Hawke, hawke, hawke!! My god he could make anyone go against anything they’ve ever believed haha and I wouldn’t have a regret in the world! Is Hawke at the top of my book boyfriend list? Absolutely!<br /><br />The MC in this book was very likeable and I felt like I related to her character in a lot of ways. Poppy had flaws that she was self conscious about but she pushed through that and learned that there’s nothing wrong with them. She was smart, innocent in a lot of ways and a bad ass who could defend herself! And I loved her for it!<br /><br />I figured out the plot twist before it was revealed but it still kept me on the edge of my seat and kept my heart racing. My mouth dropped at that ending and I’m guessing this is going to be a duology or maybe even a series? I definitely have to check out more books by the author to hold me until the release of the next book! <br /><br />Please I’m begging everyone to pick this book up. You will NOT be disappointed!!<br /><br /><b>5/5 🌟’s</b></span>

<div id="review_3460982408" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3460982408" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40997852-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605132719p2/40997852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3460982408?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/40997852-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3460982408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2341673099909182042">When I picked up this book, I did not expect to enjoy it so much. Even though it’s over 600 pages, I flew through it because it had this addicting quality –especially when Hawke was introduced. Well, I did not lose hope completely in JLA, I hope she writes more of this genre. <br/>Which includes: NA + fantasy => me drooling <br/><br/>I don’t like providing a summary of the events when there’s a GR summary that’ll do a better job AND free of typos. But basically we have Poppy, the Maiden, chosen to serve the go</span>
  <span id="freeText2341673099909182042" style="display:none">When I picked up this book, I did not expect to enjoy it so much. Even though it’s over 600 pages, I flew through it because it had this addicting quality –especially when Hawke was introduced. Well, I did not lose hope completely in JLA, I hope she writes more of this genre. <br />Which includes: NA + fantasy =&gt; me drooling <br /><br />I don’t like providing a summary of the events when there’s a GR summary that’ll do a better job AND free of typos. But basically we have Poppy, the Maiden, chosen to serve the gods, aka she’s not to socialize and lives a very sheltered life. But she’s hungry for more. And then we have her bodyguard. Hawke Flynn. The gorgeous killer. So much for a summary, I know but I’m too lazy to provide a detailed one, most of the plot revolves around those two.<br /><br />Now without talking too much, I’ll directly jump to the pros and cons:<br /><b>Pros</b><br />✎ Hawke, yes he did some questionable things but I don’t care? I adored him<br />✎ The romance, the slow burn killed me<br />✎ I also liked Poppy, she’s awesome and badass<br />✎ the smut<br />✎ We also had some lovable secondary characters like Vikter and Tawny <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I kept assuming Tawny will betray her for some reason, I’m glad she didn’t <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Okay, that’s a very short list but hey, that’s <i>why</i> I read this book from the start not for the famed outstanding world-building…<br /><br />Before I move on to the cons, I want to add a few things that aren’t necessarily bad nor good.<br />There’s a strong foreshadowing that I was only surprised by one thing throughout this book (and if I wasn’t too focused on Poppy and Hawke’s interactions, I would’ve seen it coming as well). Of course, I didn’t have everything figured out but I saw the direction this book was taking and then when this surprising event happened, everything clicked into place. So if you’re expecting mindblowing twists, turn back, this isn’t for you. <br /><br /><b>Now to the cons</b><br />✎ The slow start. It dragged a lot and it wasn’t all necessary. When a book is over 600 pages –especially when it comes to this genre- I expected a valid reason. From Blood and Ash didn’t have any.<br />✎ The info-dump at the start. The character would be saying something only to delve upon a history lesson. And all at the beginning? It was too much. <br />✎ The monologues (too much self-reflection for my taste)<br />So as you see, I didn’t have many issues with the book. After Hawke showed up, the pace increased rapidly. <br /><br />I only recommend this book if you’re looking for a specific read: a hot romance in a fantasy world. I made it sound like the romance is the center of the plot but it’s not, it’s actually Poppy’s journey to the Ascension –when she will be meeting the gods to become an immortal. With romance along the way. But it’s clear by now which part interested me the most. I can hardly wait to read the sequel. And it’ll be released the next month. Yey.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2341673099909182042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_35702241'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35702241-the-shadows-between-us"><img alt="The Shadows Between Us" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1558027905l/35702241._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Zt7w/oeTR374wgBfTDHSw880iNaHzL6KABUHtZP4SOQ/HTjz/7LqQhEb9EGnZ8ORsPOJDeWzFUsLIzSJqGQXYA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('htwAOuFToYXEnRS5Rkfeo/Sgls8M7ceTdO0qVCgFiCrfH8g3mXIMuS1E4KetEc/xi2eXFG6SbFJ/2xloE5nXrg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

All the rumors yo</span>
  <span id="freeText11151809032713215264" style="display:none">Hey Guys! Please note: I don't send out ARCs for review. If you're interested in reviewing a book of mine before release date, please contact the appropriate publisher. I also do NOT check my Goodreads email.<br /><br />To email me, please use the below addy. <br />jenniferlarmentrout@live.com<br /><br /># 1 New York Times and # 1 International Bestselling author Jennifer lives in Charles Town, West Virginia. All the rumors you’ve heard about her state aren’t true. When she’s not hard at work writing. she spends her time reading, watching really bad zombie movies, pretending to write, hanging out with her husband and her Jack Russell Loki. In early 2015, Jennifer was diagnosed with retinitis pigmentosa, a group of rare genetic disorders that involve a breakdown and death of cells in the retina, eventually resulting in loss of vision, among other complications. Due to this diagnosis, educating people on the varying degrees of blindness has become of passion of hers, right alongside writing, which she plans to do as long as she can. <br /><br />Her dreams of becoming an author started in algebra class, where she spent most of her time writing short stories….which explains her dismal grades in math. Jennifer writes young adult paranormal, science fiction, fantasy, and contemporary romance. She is published with Tor, HarperCollins Avon and William Morrow, Entangled Teen and Brazen, Disney/Hyperion and Harlequin Teen. Her Wicked Series has been optioned by PassionFlix. Jennifer has won numerous awards, including the 2013 Reviewers Choice Award for Wait for You, the 2015 Editor’s Pick for Fall With Me, and the 2014/2015 Moerser-Jugendbuch- Jury award for Obsidian. Her young adult romantic suspense novel DON’T LOOK BACK was a 2014 nominated Best in Young Adult Fiction by YALSA. Her adult romantic suspense novel TILL DEATH was a Amazon Editor’s Pick and iBook Book of the Month. Her young adult contemporary THE PROBLEM WITH FOREVER is a 2017 RITA Award Winner in Young Adult Fiction. She also writes Adult and New Adult contemporary and paranormal romance under the name J. Lynn. She is published by Entangled Brazen and HarperCollins.<br /><br />She is the owner of ApollyCon and The Origin Event, the successful annual events that features over hundred bestselling authors in Young Adult, New Adult, and Adult Fiction, panels, parties, and more.</span>
